he say , and when he speak her name it sound a if he speak the name of one dead .
After a little the bad sting pass away .
He refuse to believe long that Blossom would be ashamed of him ; he know she would not .
Three year could not so alter her loyal nature -- no , nor ten time three year .
But she would be change -- she would have grow away from him in those three busy , brilliant year .
His companionship could no longer satisfy her .
How simple and childish he have be to expect it !
She would be sweet and kind -- Blossom could never be anything else .
She would not show open discontent or dissatisfaction ; she would not be like Lauretta Bradley ; but it would be there , and he would divine it , and it would break his heart .
Mrs. Blewett be right .
When he have give Blossom up he should not have make a half-hearted thing of his sacrifice -- he should not have bind her to come back to him .
He walk about in his little garden until late at night , under the star , with the sea crooning and call to him down the slope .
When he finally go to bed he do not sleep , but lay until morning with tear-wet eye and despair in his heart .
All the forenoon he go about his usual daily work absently .
Frequently he fell into long revery , stand motionless wherever he happen to be , and look dully before him .
Only once do he show any animation .
When he saw Mrs. Blewett come up the lane he dart into the house , lock the door , and listen to her knocking in grim silence .
After she have go he go out , and find a plate of fresh doughnut , cover with a napkin , place on the bench at the door .
Mrs. Blewett mean to indicate thus that she bore him no malice for her curt dismissal the day before ; possibly her conscience give her some twinge also .
But her doughnut could not minister to the mind she have diseased .
Old Man Shaw take them up ; carry them to the pig-pen , and feed them to the pig .
It be the first spiteful thing he have do in his life , and he felt a most immoral satisfaction in it .
In mid-afternoon he go out to the garden , find the new loneliness of the little house unbearable .
The old bench be warm in the sunshine .
Old Man Shaw sit down with a long sigh , and drop his white head wearily on his breast .
He have decide what he must do .
He would tell Blossom that she might go back to her aunt and never mind about him -- he would do very well by himself and he do not blame her in the least .
He be still sit broodingly there when a girl come up the lane .
She be tall and straight , and walk with a kind of uplift in her motion , a if it would be rather easy to fly than not .
She be dark , with a rich dusky sort of darkness , suggestive of the bloom on purple plum , or the glow of deep red apple among bronze leaf .
Her big brown eye linger on everything in sight , and little gurgle of sound now and again come through her parted lip , a if inarticulate joy be thus express itself .
At the garden gate she saw the bent figure on the old bench , and the next minute she be fly along the rise walk .
`` Daddy ! ''
she call , `` daddy ! ''
Old Man Shaw stand up in hasty bewilderment ; then a pair of girlish arm be about his neck , and a pair of warm red lip be on his ; girlish eye , full of love , be look up into his , and a never-forgotten voice , tingle with laughter and tear blend into one delicious chord , be cry , `` Oh , daddy , be it really you ?
Oh , I ca n't tell you how good it be to see you again ! ''
Old Man Shaw hold her tightly in a silence of amazement and joy too deep for wonder .
Why , this be his Blossom -- the very Blossom who have go away three year ago !
A little taller , a little more womanly , but his own dear Blossom , and no stranger .
There be a new heaven and a new earth for him in the realization .
`` Oh , Baby Blossom ! ''
he murmur , `` Little Baby Blossom ! ''
Sara rub her cheek against the faded coat sleeve .
`` Daddy darling , this moment make up for everything , do n't it ? ''
`` But -- but -- where do you come from ? ''
he ask , his sens begin to struggle out of their bewilderment of surprise .
`` I do n't expect you till to-morrow .
You do n't have to walk from the station , do you ?
And your old daddy not there to welcome you ! ''
Sara laugh , swing herself back by the tip of her finger and dance around him in the childish fashion of long ago .
`` I find I could make an early connection with the C.P.A . yesterday and get to the Island last night .
I be in such a fever to get home that I jump at the chance .
Of course I walk from the station -- it 's only two mile and every step be a benediction .
My trunk be over there .
We 'll go after them to-morrow , daddy , but just now I want to go straight to every one of the dear old nook and spot at once . ''
`` You must get something to eat first , '' he urge fondly .
`` And there ai n't much in the house , I 'm afraid .
I be go to bake to-morrow morning .
But I guess I can forage you out something , darling . ''
He be sorely repent have give Mrs. Blewett 's doughnut to the pig , but Sara brush all such consideration aside with a wave of her hand .
`` I do n't want anything to eat just now .
By and by we 'll have a snack ; just a we use to get up for ourselves whenever we felt hungry .

Let u begin right here with the garden .
Oh , daddy , by what witchcraft have you coax that sulky rose-bush into bloom ? ''
`` No witchcraft at all -- it just bloom because you be come home , baby , '' say her father .
They have a glorious afternoon of it , those two child .
They explore the garden and then the house .

`` Oh , it 's lovely to see my little room again , daddy .
I 'm sure all my old hope and dream be wait here for me . ''

I 've look at magnificent scenery -- and then I 'd shut my eye and conjure up that picture .

How I 've long for that music ! ''
He take her to the orchard and follow out his crafty plan of surprise perfectly .
She reward him by do exactly what he have dream of her do , clap her hand and cry out : `` Oh , daddy !
Why , daddy ! ''
They finish up with the shore , and then at sunset they come back and sit down on the old garden bench .
Before them a sea of splendour , burn like a great jewel , stretch to the gateway of the west .
The long headland on either side be darkly purple , and the sun leave behind him a vast , cloudless arc of fiery daffodil and elusive rise .
Back over the orchard in a cool , green sky glimmer a crystal planet , and the night pour over them a clear wine of dew from her airy chalice .
The spruce be rejoice in the wind , and even the batter fir be sing of the sea .
Old memory troop into their heart like shin spirit .
`` Baby Blossom , '' say Old Man Shaw falteringly , `` be you quite sure you 'll be content here ?
Out there '' -- with a vague sweep of his hand towards horizon that shut out a world far remove from White Sands -- `` there 's pleasure and excitement and all that .
Wo n't you miss it ?
Wo n't you get tire of your old father and White Sands ? ''
Sara pat his hand gently .
`` The world out there be a good place , '' she say thoughtfully , `` I 've have three splendid year and I hope they 'll enrich my whole life .
There be wonderful thing out there to see and learn , fine , noble people to meet , beautiful deed to admire ; but , '' she wind her arm about his neck and lay her cheek against his -- `` there be no daddy ! ''
And Old Man Shaw look silently at the sunset -- or , rather , through the sunset to still grander and more radiant splendour beyond , of which the thing see be only the pale reflection , not worthy of attention from those who have the gift of further sight .
VII .
Aunt Olivia 's Beau Aunt Olivia tell Peggy and me about him on the afternoon we go over to help her gather her late rose for pot-pourri .

say Mr. Malcolm MacPherson -- not profanely or angrily , but a in sheer bewilderment .

It 's careless enough I be -- the west be n't a good place to learn finicky way -- but you can teach me .
You 're not go to throw me over because I track mud in ! ''

`` You ca n't be mean it ! ''
he exclaim , because he be begin to understand that she do mean it , although it be impossible for his man mind to understand anything else about the puzzle .
`` Nillie , it 's break my heart you be !
I 'll do anything -- go anywhere -- be anything you want -- only do n't be go back on me like this . ''
`` I can not marry you , Mr. MacPherson , '' say Aunt Olivia for the fourth time .
`` Nillie ! ''
exclaim Mr. Malcolm MacPherson .
There be such real agony in his tone that Peggy and I be suddenly stricken with contrition .
What be we do ?
We have no right to be listen to this pitiful interview .
The pain and protest in his voice have suddenly banish all the humour from it , and leave naught but the bare , stark tragedy .
We rise and tiptoe out of the room , wholesomely ashamed of ourselves .
When Mr. Malcolm MacPherson have go , after an hour of useless pleading , Aunt Olivia come up to u , pale and prim and determine , and tell u that there be to be no wedding .
We could not pretend surprise , but Peggy venture a faint protest .
`` Oh , Aunt Olivia , do you think you have do right ? ''
`` It be the only thing I could do , '' say Aunt Olivia stonily .
`` I could not marry Mr. Malcolm MacPherson and I tell him so .
Please tell your father -- and kindly say nothing more to me about the matter . ''
Then Aunt Olivia go downstairs , get a broom , and sweep up the mud Mr. Malcolm MacPherson have track over the step .

We felt very flat , but there be nothing to be do or say .
Father laugh at the whole thing , but I could not laugh .
I be sorry for Mr. Malcolm MacPherson and , though I be angry with her , I be sorry for Aunt Olivia , too .
Plainly she felt badly enough over her vanished hope and plan , but she have develop a strange and baffle reserve which nothing could pierce .
`` It 's nothing but a chronic case of old-maidism , '' say father impatiently .
Things be very dull for a week .
We saw no more of Mr. Malcolm MacPherson and we miss him dreadfully .
Aunt Olivia be inscrutable , and work with fierceness at superfluous task .
One evening father come home with some news .
`` Malcolm MacPherson be leave on the 7:30 train for the west , '' he say .
`` He have rent the Avonlea place and he 's off .
They say he be mad a a hatter at the trick Olivia play on him . ''

She be sew a for dear life , and her face be prim and colder than ever .

Delicacy forbid me to mention it but Peggy have no such scruple .

`` You wo n't be bother with him again .
He be leave on the mail train for the west . ''

I have never see anything like the transformation that come over her .
It be so thorough and sudden a to be almost uncanny .
The old maid vanish completely , and in her place be a woman , full to the lip with primitive emotion and pain .
`` What shall I do ? ''
she cry in a terrible voice .
`` Mary -- Peggy -- what shall I do ? ''
It be almost a shriek .
Peggy turn pale .
`` Do you care ? ''
she say stupidly .
`` Care !
Girls , I shall DIE if Malcolm MacPherson go away !
I have be mad -- I must have be mad .

But I think he would come back !
I must see him -- there be time to reach the station before the train go if I go by the field . ''
She take a wild step towards the door , but I catch her back with a sudden mind-vision of Aunt Olivia fly bareheaded and distraught across the field .
`` Wait a moment , Aunt Olivia .
Peggy , run home and get father to harness Dick in the buggy as quickly a he can .
We 'll drive Aunt Olivia to the station .
We 'll get you there in time , Aunty . ''
Peggy fly , and Aunt Olivia dash upstairs .
I linger behind to pick up her sewing , and when I get to her room she have her hat and cape on .

Rings , three brooch , a locket , three chain and a watch all go on -- anyway and anyhow .
A wonderful sight it be to see Aunt Olivia bedizen like that !
`` I would never wear them before -- but I 'll put them all on now to show him I 'm sorry , '' she gasp , with tremble lip .
When the three of u crowd into the buggy , Aunt Olivia grasp the whip before we could prevent her and , lean out , give poor Dick such a lash a he have never felt in his life before .
He go tear down the steep , stony , fast-darkening road in a fashion which make Peggy and me cry out in alarm .
Aunt Olivia be usually the most timid of woman , but now she do n't seem to know what fear be .
She keep whip and urge poor Dick the whole way to the station , quite oblivious to our assurance that there be plenty of time .
The people who meet u that night must have think we be quite mad .
I hold on the rein , Peggy grip the swaying side of the buggy , and Aunt Olivia bent forward , hat and hair blow back from her set face with it strangely crimson cheek , and ply the whip .
In such a guise do we whirl through the village and over the two-mile station road .
When we drive up to the station , where the train be shunt amid the shadow , Aunt Olivia make a fly leap from the buggy and ran along the platform , with her cape stream behind her and all her brooch and chain glitter in the light .
I toss the rein to a boy stand near and we follow .
Just under the glare of the station lamp we saw Mr. Malcolm MacPherson , grip in hand .
Fortunately no one else be very near , but it would have be all the same have they be the centre of a crowd .
Aunt Olivia fairly fling herself against him .
`` Malcolm , '' she cry , `` do n't go -- do n't go -- I 'll marry you -- I 'll go anywhere -- and I do n't care how much mud you bring in ! ''
That truly Aunt Olivia touch relieve the tension of the situation a little .
Mr. MacPherson put his arm about her and draw her back into the shadow .
`` There , there , '' he soothe .
`` Of course I wo n't be go .
Do n't cry , Nillie-girl . ''
`` And you 'll come right back with me now ? ''
implored Aunt Olivia , cling to him a if she fear he would be whisk away from her yet if she let go for a moment .
`` Of course , of course , '' he say .
Peggy get a chance home with a friend , and Aunt Olivia and Mr. Malcolm MacPherson and I drive back in the buggy .
Mr. MacPherson hold Aunt Olivia on his knee because there be no room , but she would have sit there , I think , have there be a dozen vacant seat .
She cling to him in the most barefaced fashion , and all her former primness and reserve be sweep away completely .
She kiss him a dozen time or more and tell him she love him -- and I do not even smile , nor do I want to .
Somehow , it do not seem in the least funny to me then , nor do it now , although it doubtless will to others .
There be too much real intensity of feeling in it all to leave any room for the ridiculous .
So wrap up in each other be they that I do not even feel superfluous .
I set them safely down in Aunt Olivia 's yard and turn homeward , completely forget by the pair .
But in the moonlight , which flood the front of the house , I saw something that testify eloquently to the transformation in Aunt Olivia .
It have rain that afternoon and the yard be muddy .
Nevertheless , she go in at her front door and take Mr. Malcolm MacPherson in with her without even a glance at the scraper !
VIII .
The Quarantine at Alexander Abraham 's I refuse to take that class in Sunday School the first time I be ask .
It be not that I object to teach in the Sunday School .
On the contrary I rather like the idea ; but it be the Rev . Mr. Allan who ask me , and it have always be a matter of principle with me never to do anything a man ask me to do if I could help it .
I be note for that .
It save a great deal of trouble and it simplify everything beautifully .
I have always dislike men .
It must have be bear in me , because , a far back a I can remember , an antipathy to men and dog be one of my strong characteristic .
I be note for that .
My experience through life only serve to deepen it .
The more I saw of men , the more I like cat .
So , of course , when the Rev . Allan ask me if I would consent to take a class in Sunday School , I say no in a fashion calculate to chasten him wholesomely .
If he have send his wife the first time , a he do the second , it would have be wise .
People generally do what Mrs. Allan ask them to do because they know it save time .
Mrs. Allan talk smoothly for half an hour before she mention the Sunday School , and pay me several compliment .
Mrs. Allan be famous for her tact .
Tact be a faculty for meander around to a give point instead of make a bee-line .
I have no tact .
I be note for that .
As soon a Mrs. Allan 's conversation come in sight of the Sunday School , I , who know all along whither it be tend , say , straight out , `` What class do you want me to teach ? ''
Mrs. Allan be so surprised that she forget to be tactful , and answer plainly for once in her life , `` There be two class -- one of boy and one of girl -- need a teacher .
I have be teach the girl ' class , but I shall have to give it up for a little time on account of the baby 's health .
You may have your choice , Miss MacPherson . ''
`` Then I shall take the boy , '' I say decidedly .
I be note for my decision .
`` Since they have to grow up to be men it 's well to train them properly betimes .
Nuisances they be bind to become under any circumstance ; but if they be take in hand young enough they may not grow up to be such nuisance a they otherwise would and that will be some unfortunate woman 's gain . ''
Mrs. Allan look dubious .
I know she have expect me to choose the girl .
`` They be a very wild set of boy , '' she say .
`` I never know boy who be n't , '' I retort .
`` I -- I -- think perhaps you would like the girl best , '' say Mrs. Allan hesitatingly .
If it have not be for one thing -- which I would never in this world have admit to Mrs. Allan -- I might have like the girl ' class best myself .
But the truth be , Anne Shirley be in that class ; and Anne Shirley be the one living human be that I be afraid of .
Not that I dislike her .
But she have such a habit of ask weird , unexpected question , which a Philadelphia lawyer could n't answer .
Miss Rogerson have that class once and Anne rout her , horse , foot and artillery .
I be n't go to undertake a class with a walk interrogation point in it like that .
Besides , I think Mrs. Allan require a slight snub .
Ministers ' wife be rather apt to think they can run everything and everybody , if they be not wholesomely correct now and again .
`` It be not what I like best that must be consider , Mrs. Allan , '' I say rebukingly .
`` It be what be best for those boy .
I feel that I shall be best for THEM . ''
`` Oh , I 've no doubt of that , Miss MacPherson , '' say Mrs. Allan amiably .
It be a fib for her , minister 's wife though she be .
She HAD doubt .
She think I would be a dismal failure a teacher of a boy ' class .
But I be not .
I be not often a dismal failure when I make up my mind to do a thing .
I be note for that .
`` It be wonderful what a reformation you have work in that class , Miss MacPherson -- wonderful , '' say the Rev . Mr. Allan some week later .
He do n't mean to show how amaze a thing he think it that an old maid note for be a man hater should have manage it , but his face betray him .
`` Where do Jimmy Spencer live ? ''
I ask him crisply .
`` He come one Sunday three week ago and have n't be back since .
I mean to find out why . ''
Mr. Allan cough .
`` I believe he be hire a handy boy with Alexander Abraham Bennett , out on the White Sands road , '' he say .
`` Then I be go out to Alexander Abraham Bennett 's on the White Sands road to see why Jimmy Spencer do n't come to Sunday school , '' I say firmly .
Mr. Allan 's eye twinkle ever so slightly .
I have always insist that if that man be not a minister he would have a sense of humour .
`` Possibly Mr. Bennett will not appreciate your kind interest !
He have -- ah -- a singular aversion to your sex , I understand .
No woman have ever be know to get inside of Mr. Bennett 's house since his sister die twenty year ago . ''
`` Oh , he be the one , be he ? ''
I say , remember .
`` He be the woman hater who threaten that if a woman come into his yard he 'll chase her out with a pitch-fork .
Well , he will not chase ME out ! ''
Mr. Allan give a chuckle -- a ministerial chuckle , but still a chuckle .
It irritate me slightly , because it seem to imply that he think Alexander Abraham Bennett would be one too many for me .
But I do not show Mr. Allan that he annoy me .
It be always a great mistake to let a man see that he can vex you .
The next afternoon I harness my sorrel pony to the buggy and drive down to Alexander Abraham Bennett 's .
As usual , I take William Adolphus with me for company .
William Adolphus be my favourite among my six cat .
He be black , with a white dicky and beautiful white paw .
He sit up on the seat beside me and look far more like a gentleman than many a man I 've see in a similar position .
Alexander Abraham 's place be about three mile along the White Sands road .
I know the house as soon a I come to it by it neglected appearance .
It need paint badly ; the blind be crook and tear ; weed grow up to the very door .
Plainly , there be no woman about THAT place .
Still , it be a nice house , and the barn be splendid .
My father always say that when a man 's barn be big than his house it be a sign that his income exceed his expenditure .
So it be all right that they should be big ; but it be all wrong that they should be trim and well paint .
Still , think I , what else could you expect of a woman hater ?
`` But Alexander Abraham evidently know how to run a farm , even it he be a woman hater , '' I remark to William Adolphus a I get out and tie the pony to the railing .
I have drive up to the house from the back way and now I be opposite a side door open on the veranda .
I think I might as well go to it , so I tuck William Adolphus under my arm and march up the path .
Just a I be half-way up , a dog swoop around the front corner and make straight for me .
He be the ugly dog I have ever see ; and he do n't even bark -- just come silently and speedily on , with a business-like eye .
I never stop to argue matter with a dog that do n't bark .
I know when discretion be the good part of valour .
Firmly clasp William Adolphus , I run -- not to the door , because the dog be between me and it , but to a big , low-branching cherry tree at the back corner of the house .
I reach it in time and no more .
First thrust William Adolphus on to a limb above my head , I scramble up into that bless tree without stop to think how it might look to Alexander Abraham if he happen to be watch .
My time for reflection come when I find myself perch half way up the tree with William Adolphus beside me .
William Adolphus be quite calm and unruffled .
I can hardly say with truthfulness what I be .
On the contrary , I admit that I felt considerably upset .
The dog be sit on his haunch on the ground below , watch u , and it be quite plain to be see , from his leisurely manner , that it be not his busy day .
He bar his teeth and growl when he catch my eye .
`` You LOOK like a woman hater 's dog , '' I tell him .
I mean it for an insult ; but the beast take it for a compliment .
Then I set myself to solve the question , `` How be I to get out of this predicament ? ''
It do not seem easy to solve it .
`` Shall I scream , William Adolphus ? ''
I demand of that intelligent animal .
William Adolphus shake his head .
This be a fact .
And I agree with him .
`` No , I shall not scream , William Adolphus , '' I say .
`` There be probably no one to hear me except Alexander Abraham , and I have my painful doubt about his tender mercy .
Now , it be impossible to go down .
Is it , then , William Adolphus , possible to go up ? ''
I look up .
Just above my head be an open window with a tolerably stout branch extend right across it .
`` Shall we try that way , William Adolphus ? ''
I ask .
William Adolphus , waste no word , begin to climb the tree .
I follow his example .
The dog run in circle about the tree and look thing not lawful to be utter .
It probably would have be a relief to him to bark if it have n't be so against his principle .
I get in by the window easily enough , and find myself in a bedroom the like of which for disorder and dust and general awfulness I have never see in all my life .
But I do not pause to take in detail .
With William Adolphus under my arm I march downstairs , fervently hop I should meet no one on the way .
I do not .
The hall below be empty and dusty .
I open the first door I come to and walk boldly in .
A man be sit by the window , look moodily out .
I should have know him for Alexander Abraham anywhere .
He have just the same uncared-for , ragged appearance that the house have ; and yet , like the house , it seem that he would not be bad look if he be trim up a little .
His hair look a if it have never be comb , and his whisker be wild in the extreme .
He look at me with blank amazement in his countenance .
`` Where be Jimmy Spencer ? ''
I demand .
`` I have come to see him . ''
`` How do he ever let you in ? ''
ask the man , star at me .
`` He do n't let me in , '' I retort .
`` He chase me all over the lawn , and I only save myself from be tear piecemeal by scramble up a tree .
You ought to be prosecute for keep such a dog !
Where be Jimmy ? ''
Instead of answer Alexander Abraham begin to laugh in a most unpleasant fashion .
`` Trust a woman for get into a man 's house if she have make up her mind to , '' he say disagreeably .
Seeing that it be his intention to vex me I remain cool and collect .
`` Oh , I be n't particular about get into your house , Mr. Bennett , '' I say calmly .
`` I have but little choice in the matter .
It be get in l a bad fate befall me .
It be not you or your house I want to see -- although I admit that it be worth see if a person be anxious to find out how dirty a place CAN be .
It be Jimmy .
For the third and last time -- where be Jimmy ? ''
`` Jimmy be not here , '' say Mr. Bennett gruffly -- but not quite so assuredly .
`` He leave last week and hire with a man over at Newbridge . ''
`` In that case , '' I say , pick up William Adolphus , who have be explore the room with a disdainful air , `` I wo n't disturb you any long .
I shall go . ''
`` Yes , I think it would be the wise thing , '' say Alexander Abraham -- not disagreeably this time , but reflectively , a if there be some doubt about the matter .
`` I 'll let you out by the back door .
Then the -- ahem !
-- the dog will not interfere with you .
Please go away quietly and quickly . ''
I wonder if Alexander Abraham think I would go away with a whoop .
But I say nothing , think this the most dignified course of conduct , and I follow him out to the kitchen a quickly and quietly a he could have wish .
Such a kitchen !
Alexander Abraham open the door -- which be lock -- just a a buggy contain two men drive into the yard .
`` Too late ! ''
he exclaim in a tragic tone .
I understand that something dreadful must have happen , but I do not care , since , a I fondly suppose , it do not concern me .
I push out past Alexander Abraham -- who be look as guilty a if he have be catch burglarize -- and come face to face with the man who have spring from the buggy .
It be old Dr. Blair , from Carmody , and he be look at me a if he have find me shoplift .
`` My dear Peter , '' he say gravely , `` I be VERY sorry to see you here -- very sorry indeed . ''
I admit that this exasperate me .
Besides , no man on earth , not even my own family doctor , have any right to `` My dear Peter '' me !
`` There be no loud call for sorrow , doctor , '' I say loftily .
`` If a woman , forty-eight year of age , a member of the Presbyterian church in good and regular standing , can not call upon one of her Sunday School scholar without wreck all the propriety , how old must she be before she can ? ''
The doctor do not answer my question .
Instead , he look reproachfully at Alexander Abraham .
`` Is this how you keep your word , Mr. Bennett ? ''
he say .
`` I think that you promise me that you would not let anyone into the house . ''
`` I do n't let her in , '' growl Mr. Bennett .

What be to be do with a woman like that ? ''

I be go at once . ''

This house be under quarantine for smallpox .
You will have to stay here . ''
Smallpox !
For the first and last time in my life , I openly lose my temper with a man .
I wheel furiously upon Alexander Abraham .
`` Why do n't you tell me ? ''
I cry .
`` Tell you ! ''
he say , glare at me .
`` When I first saw you it be too late to tell you .
I think the kind thing I could do be to hold my tongue and let you get away in happy ignorance .
This will teach you to take a man 's house by storm , madam ! ''

Mr. Bennett be in town yesterday -- where , a you be aware , there be a bad outbreak of smallpox -- and take dinner in a boarding-house where one of the maid be ill .
Last night she develop unmistakable symptom of smallpox .
The Board of Health at once get after all the people who be in the house yesterday , so far a they could locate them , and put them under quarantine .
I come down here this morning and explain the matter to Mr. Bennett .
I bring Jeremiah Jeffries to guard the front of the house and Mr. Bennett give me his word of honour that he would not let anyone in by the back way while I go to get another policeman and make all the necessary arrangement .
I have bring Thomas Wright and have secure the service of another man to attend to Mr. Bennett 's barn work and bring provision to the house .

It be the most distressing predicament I have ever get into in my life , but there be no sense in make it bad .

`` Yes , I be vaccinate a month ago , when the news of the smallpox first come .

Tell her to give them new milk twice a day and a square inch of butter apiece once a week .
Get her to put my two dark print wrapper , some apron , and some change of underclothing in my third best valise and have it send down to me .
My pony be tie out there to the fence .
Please take him home .
That be all , I think . ''

`` Send that cat home , too .
I wo n't have a cat around the place -- I 'd rather have smallpox . ''
I look Alexander Abraham over gradually , in a way I have , begin at his foot and travel up to his head .
I take my time over it ; and then I say , very quietly .

Anyway , you 'll have to have William Adolphus .
He be under quarantine as well a you and I . Do you suppose I be go to have my cat range at large through Avonlea , scatter smallpox germ among innocent people ?

You will have to endure William Adolphus . ''
Alexander Abraham groan , but I could see that the way I have look him over have chasten him considerably .

I could not clean house in my new suit and a silk shirtwaist .

Presently he say , `` I be NOT curious -- but will you kindly tell me why the doctor call you Peter ? ''
`` Because that be my name , I suppose , '' I answer , shake up a cushion for William Adolphus and thereby disturb the dust of year .
Alexander Abraham cough gently .
`` Is n't that -- ahem !
-- rather a peculiar name for a woman ? ''

`` I be NOT curious , '' say Alexander Abraham , `` but would you mind tell me how you come to be call Peter ? ''
`` If I have be a boy my parent intend to call me Peter in honour of a rich uncle .
When I -- fortunately -- turn out to be a girl my mother insist that I should be call Angelina .
They give me both name and call me Angelina , but as soon a I grow old enough I decide to be call Peter .
It be bad enough , but not so bad a Angelina . ''
`` I should say it be more appropriate , '' say Alexander Abraham , intend , a I perceive , to be disagreeable .
`` Precisely , '' I agree calmly .
`` My last name be MacPherson , and I live in Avonlea .
As you be NOT curious , that will be all the information you will need about me . ''
`` Oh ! ''
Alexander Abraham look a if a light have break in on him .
`` I 've hear of you .
You -- ah -- pretend to dislike men . ''
Pretend !
Goodness only know what would have happen to Alexander Abraham just then if a diversion have not take place .
But the door open and a dog come in -- THE dog .
I suppose he have get tired wait under the cherry tree for William Adolphus and me to come down .
He be even ugly indoors than out .

He have catch sight of William Adolphus curl up on the cushion , and he start across the room to investigate him .

`` Call him off yourself , '' he retort .
`` Since you 've bring that cat here you can protect him . ''

William Adolphus could and do .
He hump his back , flatten his ear , swore once , and then make a fly leap for Mr. Riley .
William Adolphus land squarely on Mr. Riley 's brindled back and promptly take fast hold , spit and claw and caterwaul .
You never saw a more astonished dog than Mr. Riley .
With a yell of terror he bolt out to the kitchen , out of the kitchen into the hall , through the hall into the room , and so into the kitchen and round again .
With each circuit he go faster and faster , until he look like a brindled streak with a dash of black and white on top .
Such a racket and commotion I never hear , and I laugh until the tear come into my eye .
Mr. Riley fly around and around , and William Adolphus hold on grimly and clawed .

`` Woman , call off that infernal cat before he kill my dog , '' he shout above the din of yelp and yowl .
`` Oh , he wo n't kill min , '' I say reassuringly , `` and he 's go too fast to hear me if I do call him .
If you can stop the dog , Mr. Bennett , I 'll guarantee to make William Adolphus listen to reason , but there 's no use try to argue with a lightning flash . ''

I run to help him up , which only seem to enrage him far .

`` So do I , Mr. Bennett , with all my heart .
But since we be not , let u make the best of it like sensible people .
And in future you will kindly remember that my name be Miss MacPherson , NOT Woman ! ''
With this the end come and I be thankful , for the noise those two animal make be so terrific that I expect the policeman would be rush in , smallpox or no smallpox , to see if Alexander Abraham and I be try to murder each other .
Mr. Riley suddenly veer in his mad career and bolt into a dark corner between the stove and the wood-box , William Adolphus let go just in time .
There never be any more trouble with Mr. Riley after that .
A meeker , more thoroughly chasten dog you could not find .
William Adolphus have the best of it and he keep it .
Seeing that thing have calm down and that it be five o'clock I decide to get tea .
I tell Alexander Abraham that I would prepare it , if he would show me where the eatable be .
`` You need n't mind , '' say Alexander Abraham .
`` I 've be in the habit of get my own tea for twenty year . ''
`` I daresay .
But you have n't be in the habit of get mine , '' I say firmly .
`` I would n't eat anything you cook if I starve to death .
If you want some occupation , you 'd better get some salve and anoint the scratch on that poor dog 's back . ''
Alexander Abraham say something that I prudently do not hear .
Seeing that he have no information to hand out I go on an explore expedition into the pantry .
The place be awful beyond description , and for the first time a vague sentiment of pity for Alexander Abraham glimmer in my breast .
When a man have to live in such surroundings the wonder be , not that he hat woman , but that he do n't hate the whole human race .
But I get up a supper somehow .
I be note for get up supper .
The bread be from the Carmody bakery and I make good tea and excellent toast ; besides , I find a can of peach in the pantry which , a they be buy , I be n't afraid to eat .
That tea and toast mellow Alexander Abraham in spite of himself .
He eat the last crust , and do n't growl when I give William Adolphus all the cream that be leave .
Mr. Riley do not seem to want anything .
He have no appetite .
By this time the doctor 's boy have arrive with my valise .
Alexander Abraham give me quite civilly to understand that there be a spare room across the hall and that I might take possession of it .
I go to it and put on a wrapper .
There be a set of fine furniture in the room , and a comfortable bed .
But the dust !
William Adolphus have follow me in and his paw leave mark everywhere he walk .
`` Now , '' I say briskly , return to the kitchen , `` I 'm go to clean up and I shall begin with this kitchen .
You 'd better betake yourself to the sitting-room , Mr. Bennett , so a to be out of the way . ''
Alexander Abraham glare at me .
`` I 'm not go to have my house meddle with , '' he snap .
`` It suit me .
If you do n't like it you can leave it . ''
`` No , I ca n't .
That be just the trouble , '' I say pleasantly .
`` If I could leave it I should n't be here for a minute .
Since I ca n't , it simply have to be clean .
I can tolerate men and dog when I be compel to , but I can not and will not tolerate dirt and disorder .
Go into the sitting-room . ''
Alexander Abraham go .
As he close the door , I hear him say , in capital , `` WHAT AN AWFUL WOMAN ! ''
I clear that kitchen and the pantry adjoining .
It be ten o'clock when I get through , and Alexander Abraham have go to bed without deign further speech .
I lock Mr. Riley in one room and William Adolphus in another and go to bed , too .
I have never felt so dead tire in my life before .
It have be a hard day .
But I get up bright and early the next morning and get a tiptop breakfast , which Alexander Abraham condescend to eat .
When the provision man come into the yard I call to him from the window to bring me a box of soap in the afternoon , and then I tackle the sitting-room .
It take me the best part of a week to get that house in order , but I do it thoroughly .
I be note for do thing thoroughly .
At the end of the time it be clean from garret to cellar .
Alexander Abraham make no comment on my operation , though he groan loud and often , and say caustic thing to poor Mr. Riley , who have n't the spirit to answer back after his drubbing by William Adolphus .
I make allowance for Alexander Abraham because his vaccination have take and his arm be real sore ; and I cook elegant meal , not have much else to do , once I have get thing scour up .
The house be full of provision -- Alexander Abraham be n't mean about such thing , I will say that for him .
Altogether , I be more comfortable than I have expect to be .
When Alexander Abraham would n't talk I let him alone ; and when he would I just say a sarcastic thing a he do , only I say them smile and pleasant .
I could see he have a wholesome awe for me .
But now and then he seem to forget his disposition and talk like a human be .
We have one or two real interesting conversation .
Alexander Abraham be an intelligent man , though he have get terribly warp .
I tell him once I think he must have be nice when he be a boy .
One day he astonish me by appear at the dinner table with his hair brush and a white collar on .
We have a tiptop dinner that day , and I have make a pudding that be far too good for a woman hater .
When Alexander Abraham have dispose of two large plateful of it , he sigh and say , `` You can certainly cook .
It 's a pity you be such a detestable crank in other respect . ''
`` It 's kind of convenient be a crank , '' I say .
`` People be careful how they meddle with you .
Have n't you find that out in your own experience ? ''
`` I be NOT a crank , '' growl Alexander Abraham resentfully .
`` All I ask be to be let alone . ''
`` That 's the very cranky kind of crank , '' I say .
`` A person who want to be let alone fly in the face of Providence , who decree that folk for their own good be not to be let alone .
But cheer up , Mr. Bennett .
The quarantine will be up on Tuesday and then you 'll certainly be let alone for the rest of your natural life , as far a William Adolphus and I be concern .
You may then return to your wallow in the mire and be a dirty and comfortable a of yore . ''
Alexander Abraham growl again .
The prospect do n't seem to cheer him up as much a I should have expect .
Then he do an amazing thing .
He pour some cream into a saucer and set it down before William Adolphus .
William Adolphus lap it up , keep one eye on Alexander Abraham l the latter should change his mind .
Not to be outdone , I hand Mr. Riley a bone .
Neither Alexander Abraham nor I have worry much about the smallpox .
We do n't believe he would take it , for he have n't even see the girl who be sick .
But the very next morning I hear him call me from the upstairs landing .
`` Miss MacPherson , '' he say in a voice so uncommonly mild that it give me an uncanny feeling , `` what be the symptom of smallpox ? ''
`` Chills and flush , pain in the limb and back , nausea and vomiting , '' I answer promptly , for I have be read them up in a patent medicine almanac .
`` I 've get them all , '' say Alexander Abraham hollowly .
I do n't feel as much scar a I should have expect .
After endure a woman hater and a brindled dog and the early disorder of that house -- and come off best with all three -- smallpox seem rather insignificant .
I go to the window and call to Thomas Wright to send for the doctor .
The doctor come down from Alexander Abraham 's room look grave .
`` It 's impossible to pronounce on the disease yet , '' he say .
`` There be no certainty until the eruption appear .
But , of course , there be every likelihood that it be the smallpox .
It be very unfortunate .
I be afraid that it will be difficult to get a nurse .
All the nurse in town who will take smallpox case be overbusy now , for the epidemic be still rag there .
However , I 'll go into town to-night and do my best .
Meanwhile , at present , you must not go near him , Peter . ''
I be n't go to take order from any man , and as soon a the doctor have go I march straight up to Alexander Abraham 's room with some dinner for him on a tray .
There be a lemon cream I think he could eat even if he have the smallpox .
`` You should n't come near me , '' he growl .
`` You be risk your life . ''
`` I be not go to see a fellow creature starve to death , even if he be a man , '' I retort .
`` The bad of it all , '' groan Alexander Abraham , between mouthful of lemon cream , `` be that the doctor say I 've get to have a nurse .
I 've get so kind of use to you be in the house that I do n't mind you , but the thought of another woman come here be too much .
Did you give my poor dog anything to eat ? ''
`` He have have a good dinner than many a Christian , '' I say severely .
Alexander Abraham need not have worry about another woman come in .
The doctor come back that night with care on his brow .
`` I do n't know what be to be do , '' he say .
`` I ca n't get a soul to come here . '' ''
I shall nurse Mr. Bennett , '' I say with dignity .
`` It be my duty and I never shirk my duty .
I be note for that .
He be a man , and he have smallpox , and he keep a vile dog ; but I be not go to see him die for lack of care for all that . ''
`` You 're a good soul , Peter , '' say the doctor , look relieve , manlike , as soon a he find a woman to shoulder the responsibility .
I nurse Alexander Abraham through the smallpox , and I do n't mind it much .
He be much more amiable sick than well , and he have the disease in a very mild form .
Below stair I reign supreme and Mr. Riley and William Adolphus lay down together like the lion and the lamb .
I feed Mr. Riley regularly , and once , see him look lonesome , I pat him gingerly .
It be nicer than I think it would be .
Mr. Riley lift his head and look at me with an expression in his eye which cure me of wonder why on earth Alexander Abraham be so fond of the beast .
When Alexander Abraham be able to sit up , he begin to make up for the time he 'd lose be pleasant .
Anything more sarcastic than that man in his convalescence you could n't imagine .
I just laugh at him , have find out that that could be depend on to irritate him .
To irritate him still far I clean the house all over again .
But what vex him most of all be that Mr. Riley take to follow me about and wag what he have of a tail at me .
`` It be n't enough that you should come into my peaceful home and turn it upside down , but you have to alienate the affection of my dog , '' complain Alexander Abraham .
`` He 'll get fond of you again when I go home , '' I say comfortingly .
`` Dogs be n't very particular that way .
What they want be bone .
Cats now , they love disinterestedly .
William Adolphus have never swerve in his allegiance to me , although you do give him cream in the pantry on the sly . ''
Alexander Abraham look foolish .
He have n't think I know that .
I do n't take the smallpox and in another week the doctor come out and send the policeman home .
I be disinfect and William Adolphus be fumigate , and then we be free to go .
`` Good-bye , Mr. Bennett , '' I say , offer to shake hand in a forgiving spirit .
`` I 've no doubt that you be glad to be rid of me , but you be no gladder than I be to go .
I suppose this house will be dirty than ever in a month 's time , and Mr. Riley will have discard the little polish his manner have take on .
Reformation with men and dog never go very deep . ''
With this Parthian shaft I walk out of the house , suppose that I have see the last of it and Alexander Abraham .
I be glad to get back home , of course ; but it do seem queer and lonesome .
The cat hardly know me , and William Adolphus roam about forlornly and appear to feel like an exile .
I do n't take as much pleasure in cook a usual , for it seem kind of foolish to be fuss over oneself .
The sight of a bone make me think of poor Mr. Riley .
The neighbour avoid me pointedly , for they could n't get rid of the fear that I might erupt into smallpox at any moment .
My Sunday School class have be give to another woman , and altogether I felt a if I do n't belong anywhere .
I have exist like this for a fortnight when Alexander Abraham suddenly appear .
He walk in one evening at dusk , but at first sight I do n't know him he be so spruced and barber up .
But William Adolphus know him .
Will you believe it , William Adolphus , my own William Adolphus , rub up against that man 's trouser leg with an undisguised purr of satisfaction .
`` I have to come , Angelina , '' say Alexander Abraham .
`` I could n't stand it any longer . ''
`` My name be Peter , '' I say coldly , although I be feel ridiculously glad about something .
`` It be n't , '' say Alexander Abraham stubbornly .
`` It be Angelina for me , and always will be .
I shall never call you Peter .
Angelina just suit you exactly ; and Angelina Bennett would suit you still well .
You must come back , Angelina .
Mr. Riley be mop for you , and I ca n't get along without somebody to appreciate my sarcasm , now that you have accustom me to the luxury . ''
`` What about the other five cat ? ''
I demand .
Alexander Abraham sigh .
`` I suppose they 'll have to come too , '' he sigh , `` though no doubt they 'll chase poor Mr. Riley clean off the premise .
But I can live without him , and I ca n't without you .
How soon can you be ready to marry me ? ''
`` I have n't say that I be go to marry you at all , have I ? ''
I say tartly , just to be consistent .
For I be n't feeling tart .
`` No , but you will , wo n't you ? ''
say Alexander Abraham anxiously .
`` Because if you wo n't , I wish you 'd let me die of the smallpox .
Do , dear Angelina . ''
To think that a man should dare to call me his `` dear Angelina ! ''
And to think that I should n't mind !
`` Where I go , William Adolphus go , '' I say , `` but I shall give away the other five cat for -- for the sake of Mr. Riley . ''
IX .
Pa Sloane 's Purchase `` I guess the molasses be get low , ai n't it ? ''
say Pa Sloane insinuatingly .
`` S'pose I 'd well drive up to Carmody this afternoon and get some more . ''
`` There 's a good half-gallon of molasses in the jug yet , '' say ma Sloane ruthlessly .
`` That so ?
Well , I notice the kerosene demijohn be n't very hefty the last time I fill the can .
Reckon it need replenish . ''
`` We have kerosene enough to do for a fortnight yet . ''
Ma continue to eat her dinner with an impassive face , but a twinkle make itself apparent in her eye .
Lest Pa should see it , and feel encouraged thereby , she look immovably at her plate .
Pa Sloane sigh .
His invention be give out .
`` Did n't I hear you say day before yesterday that you be out of nutmeg ? ''
he query , after a few moment ' severe reflection .
`` I get a supply of them from the egg-pedlar yesterday , '' respond Ma , by a great effort prevent the twinkle from spread over her entire face .
She wonder if this third failure would squelch Pa. .
But Pa be not to be squelch .
`` Well , anyway , '' he say , brighten up under the influence of a sudden saving inspiration .
`` I 'll have to go up to get the sorrel mare shod .
So , if you 've any little errand you want do at the store , Ma , just make a memo of them while I hitch up . ''
The matter of shoe the sorrel mare be beyond Ma 's province , although she have her own suspicion about the sorrel mare 's need of shoe .
`` Why ca n't you give up beat about the bush , Pa ? ''
she demand , with contemptuous pity .
`` You might as well own up what 's take you to Carmody .
I can see through your design .
You want to get away to the Garland auction .
That be what be trouble you , Pa Sloane . ''
`` I dunno but what I might step over , see it 's so handy .
But the sorrel mare really do need shoe , Ma , '' protest Pa. .
`` There 's always something need to be do if it 's convenient , '' retort Ma .
`` Your mania for auction will be the ruin of you yet , Pa. .
A man of fifty-five ought to have grow out of such a hankering .
But the old you get the bad you get .
Anyway , if I want to go to auction , I 'd select them a be something like , and not waste my time on little one-horse affair like this of Garland 's . ''
`` One might pick up something real cheap at Garland 's , '' say Pa defensively .
`` Well , you be not go to pick up anything , cheap or otherwise , Pa Sloane , because I 'm go with you to see that you do n't .
I know I ca n't stop you from go .
I might as well try to stop the wind from blow .
But I shall go , too , out of self-defence .
This house be so full now of old clutter and truck that you 've bring home from auction that I feel a if I be make up out of piece and leave over . ''
Pa Sloane sigh again .
It be not exhilarate to attend an auction with Ma .
She would never let him bid on anything .
But he realize that Ma 's mind be make up beyond the power of mortal man 's persuasion to alter it , so he go out to hitch up .
Pa Sloane 's dissipation be go to auction and buy thing that nobody else would buy .
Ma Sloane 's patient endeavour of over thirty year have be able to effect only a partial reform .
Sometimes Pa heroically refrain from go to an auction for six month at a time ; then he would break out bad than ever , go to all that take place for mile around , and come home with a wagonful of misfit .
His last exploit have be to bid on an old dasher churn for five dollar -- the boys `` run thing up '' on Pa Sloane for the fun of it -- and bring it home to outrage Ma , who have make her butter for fifteen year in the very late , most up-to-date barrel churn .
To add insult to injury this be the second dasher churn Pa have buy at auction .
That settle it .
Ma decree that henceforth she would chaperon Pa when he go to auction .
But this be the day of Pa 's good angel .
When he drive up to the door where Ma be wait , a breathless , hatless imp of ten fly into the yard , and hurl himself between Ma and the wagon-step .
`` Oh , Mrs. Sloane , wo n't you come over to our house at once ? ''
he gasp .
`` The baby , he 's get colic , and ma 's just wild , and he 's all black in the face . ''
Ma go , feel that the star in their course fight against a woman who be try to do her duty by her husband .
But first she admonish Pa. .
`` I shall have to let you go alone .
But I charge you , Pa , not to bid on anything -- on ANYTHING , do you hear ? ''
Pa heard and promise to heed , with every intention of keep his promise .
Then he drive away joyfully .
On any other occasion Ma would have be a welcome companion .
But she certainly spoil the flavour of an auction .
When Pa arrive at the Carmody store , he saw that the little yard of the Garland place below the hill be already full of people .
The auction have evidently begin ; so , not to miss any more of it , Pa hurry down .
The sorrel mare could wait for her shoe until afterwards .
Ma have be within bound when she call the Garland auction a `` one-horse affair . ''
It certainly be very paltry , especially when compare to the big Donaldson auction of a month ago , which Pa still live over in happy dream .
Horace Garland and his wife have be poor .
When they die within six week of each other , one of consumption and one of pneumonia , they leave nothing but debt and a little furniture .
The house have be a rented one .
The bidding on the various poor article of household gear put up for sale be not brisk , but have an element of resigned determination .
Carmody people know that these thing have to be sell to pay the debt , and they could not be sell unless they be buy .
Still , it be a very tame affair .
A woman come out of the house carry a baby of about eighteen month in her arm , and sit down on the bench beneath the window .
`` There 's Marthy Blair with the Garland Baby , '' say Robert Lawson to Pa. .
`` I 'd like to know what 's to become of that poor young one ! ''
`` Ai n't there any of the father 's or mother 's folk to take him ? ''
ask Pa. .
`` No .
Horace have no relative that anybody ever heard of .
Mrs. Horace have a brother ; but he go to Mantioba year ago , and nobody know where he be now .
Somebody 'll have to take the baby and nobody seem anxious to .
I 've get eight myself , or I 'd think about it .
He 's a fine little chap . ''
Pa , with Ma 's part admonition ring in his ear , do not bid on anything , although it will never be know how great be the heroic self-restraint he put on himself , until just at the last , when he do bid on a collection of flower-pots , think he might indulge himself to that small extent .
But Josiah Sloane have be commission by his wife to bring those flower-pots home to her ; so Pa lose them .
`` There , that 's all , '' say the auctioneer , wipe his face , for the day be very warm for October .
`` There 's nothing more unless we sell the baby . ''
A laugh go through the crowd .
The sale have be a dull affair , and they be ready for some fun .
Someone call out , `` Put him up , Jacob . ''
The joke find favour and the call be repeat hilariously .
Jacob Blair take little Teddy Garland out of Martha 's arm and stand him up on the table by the door , steady the small chap with one big brown hand .
The baby have a mop of yellow curl , and a pink and white face , and big blue eye .
He laugh out at the men before him and wave his hand in delight .
Pa Sloane think he have never see so pretty a baby .
`` Here 's a baby for sale , '' shout the auctioneer .
`` A genuine article , pretty near as good a brand-new .
A real live baby , warrant to walk and talk a little .
Who bid ?
A dollar ?
Did I hear anyone mean enough to bid a dollar ?
No , sir , baby do n't come as cheap a that , especially the curly-headed brand . ''
The crowd laugh again .
Pa Sloane , by way of keep on the joke , cry , `` Four dollar ! ''
Everybody look at him .
The impression flash through the crowd that Pa be in earnest , and mean thus to signify his intention of give the baby a home .
He be well-to-do , and his only son be grow up and marry .
`` Six , '' cry out John Clarke from the other side of the yard .
John Clarke live at White Sands and he and his wife be childless .
That bid of John Clarke 's be Pa 's undoing .
Pa Sloane could not have an enemy ; but a rival he have , and that rival be John Clarke .
Everywhere at auction John Clarke be wont to bid against Pa. .
At the last auction he have outbid Pa in everything , not have the fear of his wife before his eye .
Pa 's fight blood be up in a moment ; he forget Ma Sloane ; he forget what he be bid for ; he forget everything except a determination that John Clarke should not be victor again .
`` Ten , '' he call shrilly .
`` Fifteen , '' shout Clarke .
`` Twenty , '' vociferate Pa. .
`` Twenty-five , '' bellow Clarke .
`` Thirty , '' shriek Pa. .
He nearly bust a blood-vessel in his shrieking , but he have win .
Clarke turn off with a laugh and a shrug , and the baby be knock down to Pa Sloane by the auctioneer , who have meanwhile be keep the crowd in roar of laughter by a quick fire of witticism .
There have not be such fun at an auction in Carmody for many a long day .
Pa Sloane come , or be push , forward .
The baby be put into his arm ; he realize that he be expect to keep it , and he be too daze to refuse ; besides , his heart go out to the child .
The auctioneer look doubtfully at the money which Pa lay mutely down .
`` I s ` pose that part be only a joke , '' he say .
`` Not a bit of it , '' say Robert Lawson .
`` All the money wo n't bee too much to pay the debt .
There 's a doctor 's bill , and this will just about pay it . ''
Pa Sloane drive back home , with the sorrel mare still unshod , the baby , and the baby 's meager bundle of clothes .
The baby do not trouble him much ; it have become well used to stranger in the past two month , and promptly fell asleep on his arm ; but Pa Sloane do not enjoy that drive ; at the end of it ; he mentally saw Ma Sloane .
Ma be there , too , wait for him on the back door-step a he drive into the yard at sunset .
Her face , when she saw the baby , express the last degree of amazement .
`` Pa Sloane , '' she demand , `` whose be that young one , and there do you get it ? ''
`` I -- I -- buy it at the auction , Ma , '' say Pa feebly .
Then he wait for the explosion .
None come .
This last exploit of Pa 's be too much for Ma .
With a gasp she snatch the baby from Pa 's arm , and order him to go out and put the mare in .
When Pa return to the kitchen Ma have set the baby on the sofa , fence him around with chair so that he could n't fall off and give him a molassed cooky .
`` Now , Pa Sloane , you can explain , '' she say .
Pa explain .
Ma listen in grim silence until he have finish .
Then she say sternly : `` Do you reckon we 're go to keep this baby ? ''
`` I -- I -- dunno , '' say Pa. .
And he do n't .
`` Well , we 're NOT .
I bring up one boy and that 's enough .
I do n't calculate to be pester with any more .
I never be much struck on child a child , anyhow .
You say that Mary Garland have a brother out in Mantioba ?
Well , we shall just write to him and tell him he 's get to look out for his nephew . ''
`` But how can you do that , Ma , when nobody know his address ? ''
object Pa , with a wistful look at that delicious , laugh baby .
`` I 'll find out his address if I have to advertise in the paper for him , '' retort Ma .
`` As for you , Pa Sloane , you 're not fit to be out of a lunatic asylum .
The next auction you 'll be buy a wife , I s ` pose ? ''
Pa , quite crush by Ma 's sarcasm , pull his chair in to supper .
Ma pick up the baby and sit down at the head of the table .
Little Teddy laugh and pinch her face -- Ma 's face !
Ma look very grim , but she feed him his supper as skilfully a if it have not be thirty year since she have do such a thing .
But then , the woman who once learn the mother knack never forget it .
After tea Ma despatch Pa over to William Alexander 's to borrow a high chair .
When Pa return in the twilight , the baby be fence in on the sofa again , and Ma be step briskly about the garret .
She be bring down the little cot bed her own boy have once occupy , and set it up in their room for Teddy .
Then she undress the baby and rock him to sleep , croon an old lullaby over him .
Pa Sloane sit quietly and listen , with very sweet memory of the long ago , when he and Ma have be young and proud , and the bewhiskered William Alexander have be a curly-headed little fellow like this one .
Ma be not drive to advertising for Mrs. Garland 's brother .
That personage saw the notice of his sister 's death in a home paper and write to the Carmody postmaster for full information .
The letter be refer to Ma and Ma answer it .
She write that they have take in the baby , pending further arrangement , but have no intention of keep it ; and she calmly demand of it uncle what be to be do with it .
Then she seal and address the letter with an unfaltering hand ; but , when it be do , she look across the table at Pa Sloane , who be sit in the armchair with the baby on his knee .
They be have a royal good time together .
Pa have always be dreadfully foolish about baby .
He look ten year younger .
Ma 's keen eye soften a little a she watch them .
A prompt answer come to her letter .
Teddy 's uncle write that he have six child of his own , but be nevertheless willing and glad to give his little nephew a home .
But he could not come after him .
Josiah Spencer , of White Sands , be go out to Manitoba in the spring .
If Mr. and Mrs. Sloane could only keep the baby till then he could be send out with the Spencers .
Perhaps they would see a chance sooner .
`` There 'll be no chance sooner , '' say Pa Sloane in a tone of satisfaction .
`` No , bad luck ! ''
retort Ma crisply .
The winter pass by .
Little Teddy grow and thrive , and Pa Sloane worship him .
Ma be very good to him , too , and Teddy be just a fond of her a of Pa. .
Nevertheless , a the spring draw near , Pa become depressed .
Sometimes he sigh heavily , especially when he hear casual reference to the Josiah Spencer emigration .
One warm afternoon in early May Josiah Spencer arrive .
He find Ma knit placidly in the kitchen , while Pa nod over his newspaper and the baby play with the cat on the floor .
`` Good afternoon , Mrs. Sloane , '' say Josiah with a flourish .
`` I just drop in to see about this young man here .
We be go to leave next Wednesday ; so you 'd better send him down to our place Monday or Tuesday , so that he can get use to u , and -- '' `` Oh , Ma , '' begin Pa , rise imploringly to his foot .
Ma transfix him with her eye .
`` Sit down , Pa , '' she command .
Unhappy Pa sat .
Then Ma glare at the smile Josiah , who instantly felt as guilty a if he have be catch steal sheep red-handed .
`` We be much oblige to you , Mr. Spencer , '' say Ma icily , `` but this baby be OURS .
We buy him , and we pay for him .
A bargain be a bargain .
When I pay cash down for baby , I propose to get my money 's worth .
We be go to keep this baby in spite of any number of uncle in Manitoba .
Have I make this sufficiently clear to your understanding , Mr. Spencer ? ''
`` Certainly , certainly , '' stammer the unfortunate man , feel guilty than ever , `` but I think you do n't want him -- I think you 'd write to his uncle -- I think -- '' `` I really would n't think quite so much if I be you , '' say Ma kindly .
`` It must be hard on you .
Wo n't you stay and have tea with u ? ''
But , no , Josiah would not stay .
He be thankful to make his escape with such rag of self-respect a remain to him .
Pa Sloane arise and come around to Ma 's chair .
He lay a trembling hand on her shoulder .
`` Ma , you 're a good woman , '' he say softly .
`` Go ` long , Pa , '' say Ma .
X .
The Courting of Prissy Strong I WAS N'T able to go to prayer meeting that evening because I have neuralgia in my face ; but Thomas go , and the minute he come home I know by the twinkle in his eye that he have some news .
`` Who do you s ` pose Stephen Clark go home with from meet to-night ? ''
he say , chuckle .
`` Jane Miranda Blair , '' I say promptly .
Stephen Clark 's wife have be dead for two year and he have n't take much notice of anybody , so far a be know .
But Carmody have Jane Miranda all ready for him , and really I do n't know why she do n't suit him , except for the reason that a man never do what he be expect to do when it come to marry .
Thomas chuckle again .
`` Wrong .
He step up to Prissy Strong and walk off with her .
Cold soup warm over . ''
`` Prissy Strong ! ''
I just hold up my hand .
Then I laugh .
`` He need n't try for Prissy , '' I say .
`` Emmeline nip that in the bud twenty year ago , and she 'll do it again . ''
`` Em ` line be an old crank , '' growl Thomas .
He detest Emmeline Strong , and always do .
`` She 's that , all right , '' I agree , `` and that be just the reason she can turn poor Prissy any way she like .
You mark my word , she 'll put her foot right down on this as soon a she find it out . ''
Thomas say that I be probably right .
I lay awake for a long time after I go to bed that night , thinking of Prissy and Stephen .
As a general rule , I do n't concern my head about other people 's affair , but Prissy be such a helpless creature I could n't get her off my mind .
Twenty year ago Stephen Clark have try to go with Prissy Strong .
That be pretty soon after Prissy 's father have die .
She and Emmeline be live alone together .
Emmeline be thirty , ten year old than Prissy , and if ever there be two sister totally different from each other in every way , those two be Emmeline and Prissy Strong .
Emmeline take after her father ; she be big and dark and homely , and she be the most domineering creature that ever step on shoe leather .
She simply rule poor Prissy with a rod of iron .
Prissy herself be a pretty girl -- at least most people think so .
I ca n't honestly say I ever admire her style much myself .
I like something with more vim and snap to it .
Prissy be slim and pink , with soft , appeal blue eye , and pale gold hair all clinging in baby ring around her face .
She be just a meek and timid a she look and there be n't a bit of harm in her .

He begin to drive her , and there be n't a speck of doubt that Prissy like him .

It be pure cantankerousness in her .

But she have n't a mite ; I believe she would have cut off her nose if Emmeline have order her to do it .

If ever a girl belie her name , Prissy Strong do .
There be n't anything strong about her .
One night , when prayer meeting come out , Stephen step up to Prissy a usual and ask if he might see her home .

I suppose they be afraid of Emmeline .

She be always kind of sweet look , but her bloom go , and she get shyer and limper every year of her life .

XI .
The Miracle at Carmody Salome look out of the kitchen window , and a pucker of distress appear on her smooth forehead .
`` Dear , dear , what have Lionel Hezekiah be do now ? ''
she murmur anxiously .
Involuntarily she reach out for her crutch ; but it be a little beyond her reach , have fall on the floor , and without it Salome could not move a step .
`` Well , anyway , Judith be bring him in as fast a she can , '' she reflect .
`` He must have be up to something terrible this time ; for she look very cross , and she never walk like that unless she be angry clear through .
Dear me , I be sometimes tempt to think that Judith and I make a mistake in adopt the child .
I suppose two old maid do n't know much about bring up a boy properly .
But he be NOT a bad child , and it really seem to me that there must be some way of make him behave good if we only know what it be . ''
Salome 's monologue be cut short by the entrance of her sister Judith , hold Lionel Hezekiah by his chubby wrist with a determined grip .
Judith Marsh be ten year old than Salome , and the two woman be a different in appearance a night and day .
Salome , in spite of her thirty-five year , look almost girlish .
She be small and pink and flower-like , with little ring of pale golden hair cluster all over her head in a most unspinster-like fashion , and her eye be big and blue , and mild a a dove 's .
Her face be perhaps a weak one , but it be very sweet and appeal .
Judith Marsh be tall and dark , with a plain , tragic face and iron-gray hair .
Her eye be black and sombre , and every feature bespeak unyielding will and determination .
Just now she look , a Salome have say , `` angry clear through , '' and the baleful glance she cast on the small mortal she hold would have wither a more hardened criminal than six happy-go-lucky year have make of Lionel Hezekiah .
Lionel Hezekiah , whatever his shortcoming , do not look bad .
Indeed , he be a engage an urchin a ever beam out on a jolly good world through a pair of big , velvet-brown eye .
He be chubby and firm-limbed , with a mop of beautiful golden curl , which be the despair of his heart and the pride and joy of Salome 's ; and his round face be usually a lurking-place for dimple and smile and sunshine .
But just now Lionel Hezekiah be under a blight ; he have be catch red-handed in guilt , and be feel much ashamed of himself .
He hang his head and squirm his toe under the mournful reproach in Salome 's eye .
When Salome look at him like that , Lionel Hezekiah always felt that he be pay more for his fun than it be worth .
`` What do you suppose I catch him do this time ? ''
demand Judith .
`` I -- I do n't know , '' falter Salome .
`` Firing -- at -- a -- mark -- on -- the -- henhouse -- door -- with -- new-laid -- egg , '' say Judith with measured distinctness .
`` He have break every egg that be lay to-day except three .
And a for the state of that henhouse door -- '' Judith pause , with an indignant gesture mean to convey that the state of the henhouse door must be leave to Salome 's imagination , since the English language be not capable of depict it .

say Salome miserably .

`` I -- I think it would be bully fun .
Seems 's if everything what 's fun 's wrong . ''
Salome 's heart be not proof against tear , a Lionel Hezekiah very well know .
She put her arm about the sobbing culprit , and draw him to her side .
`` He do n't know it be wrong , '' she say defiantly to Judith .
`` He 's get to be teach , then , '' be Judith 's retort .
`` No , you need n't try to beg him off , Salome .
He shall go right to bed without supper , and stay there till to-morrow morning . ''
`` Oh !
not without his supper , '' entreat Salome .
`` You -- you wo n't improve the child 's moral by injure his stomach , Judith . ''
`` Without his supper , I say , '' repeat Judith inexorably .
`` Lionel Hezekiah , go up-stairs to the south room , and go to bed at once . ''
Lionel Hezekiah go up-stairs , and go to bed at once .
He be never sulky or disobedient .
Salome listen to him a he stump patiently up-stairs with a sob at every step , and her own eye fill with tear .
`` Now do n't for pity 's sake go cry , Salome , '' say Judith irritably .
`` I think I 've let him off very easily .
He be enough to try the patience of a saint , and I never be that , '' she add with entire truth .
`` But he be n't bad , '' plead Salome .
`` You know he never do anything the second time after he have be tell it be wrong , never . ''
`` What good do that do when he be certain to do something new and twice a bad ?
I never saw anything like him for originate idea of mischief .
Just look at what he have do in the past fortnight -- in one fortnight , Salome .
He bring in a live snake , and nearly frighten you into fit ; he drink up a bottle of liniment , and almost poison himself ; he take three toad to bed with him ; he climb into the henhouse loft , and fell through on a hen and kill her ; he paint his face all over with your water-colour ; and now come THIS exploit .
And egg at twenty-eight cent a dozen !
I tell you , Salome , Lionel Hezekiah be an expensive luxury . ''
`` But we could n't do without him , '' protest Salome . ''
I could .
But a you ca n't , or think you ca n't , we 'll have to keep him , I suppose .
But the only way to secure any peace of mind for ourselves , as far a I can see , be to tether him in the yard , and hire somebody to watch him . ''
`` There must be some way of manage him , '' say Salome desperately .
She think Judith be in earnest about the tethering .
Judith be generally so terribly in earnest in all she say .
`` Perhaps it be because he have no other employment that he invent so many unheard-of thing .
If he have anything to occupy himself with -- perhaps if we send him to school -- '' `` He 's too young to go to school .
Father always say that no child should go to school until it be seven , and I do n't mean Lionel Hezekiah shall .

XII .
The End of a Quarrel Nancy Rogerson sit down on Louisa Shaw 's front doorstep and look about her , draw a long breath of delight that seem ting with pain .

INTRODUCTION It be no exaggeration to say that what Longfellow do for Acadia , Miss Montgomery have do for Prince Edward Island .
More than a million reader , young people as well a their parent and uncle and aunt , posse in the picture-galleries of their memory the exquisite landscape of Avonlea , limn with a poetic a pencil a Longfellow wield when he tell the ever-moving story of Grand Pre .
Only genius of the first water have the ability to conjure up such a character a Anne Shirley , the heroine of Miss Montgomery 's first novel , `` Anne of Green Gables , '' and to surround her with people so distinctive , so real , so true to psychology .
Anne be a lovable a child a life in all fiction .
Natasha in Count Tolstoi 's great novel , `` War and Peace , '' dance into our ken , with something of the same buoyancy and naturalness ; but into what a commonplace young woman she develop !
Anne , whether a the gay little orphan in her conquest of the master and mistress of Green Gables , or a the maturing and self-forgetful maiden of Avonlea , keep up to concert-pitch in her charm and her winsomeness .
There be nothing in her to disappoint hope or imagination .
Part of the power of Miss Montgomery -- and the large part -- be due to her skill in compound humor and pathos .
The humor be honest and golden ; it never weary the reader ; the pathos be never sentimentalize , never degenerate into bathos , be never morbid .
This combination hold throughout all her work , long or short , and be particularly manifest in the present collection of fifteen short story , which , together with those in the first volume of the Chronicles of Avonlea , present a series of piquant and fascinating picture of life in Prince Edward Island .
The humor be show not only in the presentation of quaint and unique character , but also in the word which fall from their mouth .
Aunt Cynthia `` always give you the impression of a full-rigged ship come gallantly on before a favorable wind ; '' no further description be need -- only one such personage could be find in Avonlea .
You would recognize her at sight .
Ismay Meade 's disposition be sum up when we be tell that she be `` good at have presentiment -- after thing happen . ''
What cleverer embodiment of innate obstinacy than in Isabella Spencer -- `` a wisp of a woman who look a if a breath would sway her but be so set in her way that a tornado would hardly have cause her to swerve an inch from her chosen path ; '' or than in Mrs. Eben Andrews -LRB- in `` Sara 's Way '' -RRB- who `` look like a woman whose opinion be always very decided and warrant to wear ! ''
This gift of characterization in a few word be lavish also on material object , a , for instance ; what more be need to describe the forlornness of the home from which Anne be rescue than the statement that even the tree around it `` look like orphan '' ?
The poetic touch , too , never fail in the right place and be never too frequently introduce in her description .
They throw a glamor over that Northern land which otherwise you might imagine a rather cold and barren .
What charm Springs they must have there !
One see all the fruit-trees clad in bridal garment of pink and white ; and what a translucent sky smile down on the pond and the reach of bay and cove !
`` The Eastern sky be a great arc of crystal , smite through with auroral crimsonings . ''
`` She be a slim and lithe a a young white-stemmed birch-tree ; her hair be like a soft dusky cloud , and her eye be as blue a Avonlea Harbor in a fair twilight , when all the sky be a-bloom over it . ''
Sentiment with a humorous touch to it prevail in the first two story of the present book .
The one relate to the disappearance of a valuable white Persian cat with a blue spot in it tail .

You become as much interested in Fatima 's fate a if she be your own pet , and the climax be no less unexpected than it be natural , especially when it be make also the last act of a pretty comedy of love .
Miss Montgomery delight in depict the romantic episode hide in the heart of elderly spinster a , for instance , in the case of Charlotte Holmes , whose maid Nancy would have send for the doctor and subject her to a porous plaster while wait for him , have she know that up stair there be a note-book full of original poem .

In one story , the last , `` Tannis of the Flats , '' the secret of Elinor Blair 's spinsterhood be reveal in an episode which carry the reader from Avonlea to Saskatchewan and show the unselfish devotion of a half-breed Indian girl .
The story be both poignant and dramatic .

Self-sacrifice , a the real basis of happiness , be a favorite theme in Miss Montgomery 's fiction .
It be raise to the nth power in the story entitle , `` In Her Selfless Mood , '' where an ugly , misshapen girl devote her life and renounces marriage for the sake of look after her weak and selfish half-brother .
The same spirit be find in `` Only a Common Fellow , '' who be haloed with a certain splendor by renounce the girl he be to marry in favor of his old rival , suppose to have be kill in France , but happily deliver from that tragic fate .
Miss Montgomery love to introduce a little child or a baby a a solvent of old feud or domestic quarrel .

Huldah Jane weep and be a one whom the god have make mad .

When she come back the kitchen door have blow open and Fatima have vanish .

Max come over and we have another search , but without result .
Days pass , but we do not find Fatima .
I would certainly have go crazy have it not be for Max .
He be worth his weight in gold during the awful week that follow .

`` She must have perish from exposure long ere this . ''

We have never hear of this presentiment before , but Ismay be good at have presentiment -- after thing happen .

I demand , helplessly .

If so , you must buy it , and palm it off on your good Aunt a Fatima .
She 's very short-sighted , so it will be quite possible . ''

We ask any one who have a white Persian cat , with a blue spot on the tip of it tail , to dispose of , to communicate with M. I. , care of the Enterprise .

It be a type-written screed from Halifax state that the writer have for sale a white Persian cat answer to our description .

The blue spot may be too big or too small or not in the right place .

The postmaster 's boy be there with a telegram .

cry Ismay , behold my face .

It be from Aunt Cynthia .
She have wire u to send Fatima to Halifax by express immediately .

It be I who speak first .

Neither Ismay nor I can rush off to Halifax at once .
You must go to-morrow morning .
Go right to 110 Hollis Street and ask for ` Persian . '
If the cat look enough like Fatima , buy it and take it to Aunt Cynthia .
If it do n't -- but it must !
You 'll go , wo n't you ? ''

I star at him .
This be so unlike Max .

`` How do I know that Aunt Cynthia will be deceive after all , even if she be short-sighted .
Buying a cat in a joke be a huge risk .
And if she should see through the scheme I shall be in a pretty mess . ''

demand Max sternly .

I 'll do anything , say anything -- but it must be for my future wife . ''

I say helplessly .
`` Nothing . ''
I think hard .
Of course Max be act abominably -- but -- but -- he be really a dear fellow -- and this be the twelfth time -- and there be Anne Shirley !

Besides , I would have marry him long ago have not Aunt Cynthia throw u so pointedly at each other 's head ever since he come to Spencervale .
