Next day we get a wire say it be all right .

`` So it be . '' '' '
T be n't .
You look at the address on a telegram next time you get one .
She go a week ago to visit another friend who live at 110 Hollis . ''
`` Max ! ''
`` It 's a fact .
I ring the bell , and be just go to ask the maid for ` Persian ' when your Aunt Cynthia herself come through the hall and pounce on me . '' ''

I wire them to send Fatima at once .
And she have not come yet and I be expect a call every minute from some one who want to buy her . ' ''
` Oh ! '
I murmur , mine deep every minute . ''

Fatima be really quite a charge , you know -- and so apt to die and be a dead loss , ' -- do your aunt mean a pun , girl ?
-- ` and so , although I be considerably attach to her , I have decide to part with her . '
`` By this time I have get my second wind , and I promptly decide that a judicious mixture of the truth be the thing require . ''

`` You should have see how she beam .

II .
THE MATERALIZING OF CECIL It have never worry me in the least that I be n't marry , although everybody in Avonlea pity old maid ; but it DID worry me , and I frankly confess it , that I have never have a chance to be .
Even Nancy , my old nurse and servant , know that , and pity me for it .
Nancy be an old maid herself , but she have have two proposal .
She do not accept either of them because one be a widower with seven child , and the other a very shiftless , good-for-nothing fellow ; but , if anybody twit Nancy on her single condition , she could point triumphantly to those two a evidence that `` she could an she would . ''
If I have not live all my life in Avonlea I might have have the benefit of the doubt ; but I have , and everybody know everything about me -- or think they do .
I have really often wonder why nobody have ever fall in love with me .
I be not at all homely ; indeed , year ago , George Adoniram Maybrick have write a poem address to me , in which he praise my beauty quite extravagantly ; that do n't mean anything because George Adoniram write poetry to all the good-looking girl and never go with anybody but Flora King , who be cross-eyed and red-haired , but it prove that it be not my appearance that put me out of the running .
Neither be it the fact that I write poetry myself -- although not of George Adoniram 's kind -- because nobody ever know that .
When I felt it come on I shut myself up in my room and write it out in a little blank book I keep lock up .
It be nearly full now , because I have be write poetry all my life .
It be the only thing I have ever be able to keep a secret from Nancy .
Nancy , in any case , have not a very high opinion of my ability to take care of myself ; but I tremble to imagine what she would think if she ever find out about that little book .
I be convinced she would send for the doctor post-haste and insist on mustard plaster while wait for him .
Nevertheless , I keep on at it , and what with my flower and my cat and my magazine and my little book , I be really very happy and content .
But it DID sting that Adella Gilbert , across the road , who have a drunken husband , should pity `` poor Charlotte '' because nobody have ever want her .
Poor Charlotte indeed !
If I have throw myself at a man 's head the way Adella Gilbert do at -- but there , there , I must refrain from such thought .
I must not be uncharitable .
The Sewing Circle meet at Mary Gillespie 's on my fortieth birthday .
I have give up talk about my birthday , although that little scheme be not much good in Avonlea where everybody know your age -- or if they make a mistake it be never on the side of youth .
But Nancy , who grow accustom to celebrate my birthday when I be a little girl , never get over the habit , and I do n't try to cure her , because , after all , it 's nice to have some one make a fuss over you .
She bring me up my breakfast before I get up out of bed -- a concession to my laziness that Nancy would scorn to make on any other day of the year .
She have cook everything I like best , and have decorate the tray with rose from the garden and fern from the wood behind the house .
I enjoy every bit of that breakfast , and then I get up and dress , put on my second best muslin gown .
I would have put on my really best if I have not have the fear of Nancy before my eye ; but I know she would never condone THAT , even on a birthday .
I water my flower and feed my cat , and then I lock myself up and write a poem on June .
I have give up write birthday ode after I be thirty .
In the afternoon I go to the Sewing Circle .
When I be ready for it I look in my glass and wonder if I could really be forty .
I be quite sure I do n't look it .
My hair be brown and wavy , my cheek be pink , and the line could hardly be see at all , though possibly that be because of the dim light .
I always have my mirror hung in the dark corner of my room .
Nancy can not imagine why .
I know the line be there , of course ; but when they do n't show very plain I forget that they be there .
We have a large Sewing Circle , young and old alike attending .
I really can not say I ever enjoy the meeting -- at least not up to that time -- although I go religiously because I think it my duty to go .
The married woman talk so much of their husband and child , and of course I have to be quiet on those topic ; and the young girl talk in corner group about their beau , and stop it when I join them , a if they felt sure that an old maid who have never have a beau could n't understand at all .
As for the other old maid , they talk gossip about every one , and I do not like that either .
I know the minute my back be turn they would fasten into me and hint that I use hair-dye and declare it be perfectly ridiculous for a woman of FIFTY to wear a pink muslin dress with lace-trimmed frill .
There be a full attendance that day , for we be get ready for a sale of fancy work in aid of parsonage repair .
The young girl be merry and noisy than usual .
Wilhelmina Mercer be there , and she keep them go .
The Mercers be quite new to Avonlea , have come here only two month previously .
I be sit by the window and Wilhelmina Mercer , Maggie Henderson , Susette Cross and Georgie Hall be in a little group just before me .
I be n't listen to their chatter at all , but presently Georgie exclaim teasingly : `` Miss Charlotte be laugh at u .
I suppose she think we be awfully silly to be talk about beau . ''
The truth be that I be simply smile over some very pretty thought that have come to me about the rose which be climb over Mary Gillespie 's sill .
I mean to inscribe them in the little blank book when I go home .
Georgie 's speech bring me back to harsh reality with a jolt .
It hurt me , a such speech always do .
`` Did n't you ever have a beau , Miss Holmes ? ''
say Wilhelmina laughingly .
Just a it happen , a silence have fall over the room for a moment , and everybody in it hear Wilhelmina 's question .
I really do not know what get into me and possess me .
I have never be able to account for what I say and do , because I be naturally a truthful person and hate all deceit .
It seem to me that I simply could not say `` No '' to Wilhelmina before that whole roomful of woman .
It be TOO humiliate .
I suppose all the prickle and sting and slur I have endure for fifteen year on account of never have have a lover have what the new doctor call `` a cumulative effect '' and come to a head then and there .
`` Yes , I have one once , my dear , '' I say calmly .
For once in my life I make a sensation .
Every woman in that room stop sew and star at me .
Most of them , I saw , do n't believe me , but Wilhelmina do .
Her pretty face light up with interest .
`` Oh , wo n't you tell u about him , Miss Holmes ? ''
she coax , `` and why do n't you marry him ? ''
`` That be right , Miss Mercer , '' say Josephine Cameron , with a nasty little laugh .
`` Make her tell .
We 're all interested .
It 's news to u that Charlotte ever have a beau . ''
If Josephine have not say that , I might not have go on .
But she do say it , and , moreover , I catch Mary Gillespie and Adella Gilbert exchange significant smile .
That settle it , and make me quite reckless .
`` In for a penny , in for a pound , '' think I , and I say with a pensive smile : `` Nobody here know anything about him , and it be all long , long ago . ''
`` What be his name ? ''
ask Wilhelmina .
`` Cecil Fenwick , '' I answer promptly .
Cecil have always be my favorite name for a man ; it figure quite frequently in the blank book .
As for the Fenwick part of it , I have a bit of newspaper in my hand , measure a hem , with `` Try Fenwick 's Porous Plasters '' print across it , and I simply join the two in sudden and irrevocable matrimony .
`` Where do you meet him ? ''
ask Georgie .
I hastily review my past .
There be only one place to locate Cecil Fenwick .
The only time I have ever be far enough away from Avonlea in my life be when I be eighteen and have go to visit an aunt in New Brunswick .
`` In Blakely , New Brunswick , '' I say , almost believe that I have when I saw how they all take it in unsuspectingly .
`` I be just eighteen and he be twenty-three . ''
`` What do he look like ? ''
Susette want to know .
`` Oh , he be very handsome . ''
I proceed glibly to sketch my ideal .
To tell the dreadful truth , I be enjoy myself ; I could see respect dawn in those girl ' eye , and I know that I have forever throw off my reproach .
Henceforth I should be a woman with a romantic past , faithful to the one love of her life -- a very , very different thing from an old maid who have never have a lover .
`` He be tall and dark , with lovely , curly black hair and brilliant , pierce eye .
He have a splendid chin , and a fine nose , and the most fascinating smile ! ''
`` What be he ? ''
ask Maggie .
`` A young lawyer , '' I say , my choice of profession decide by an enlarged crayon portrait of Mary Gillespie 's deceased brother on an easel before me .
He have be a lawyer .
`` Why do n't you marry him ? ''
demand Susette .
`` We quarrel , '' I answer sadly .
`` A terribly bitter quarrel .
Oh , we be both so young and so foolish .
It be my fault .
I vex Cecil by flirt with another man '' -- be n't I come on !
-- `` and he be jealous and angry .
He go out West and never come back .
I have never see him since , and I do not even know if he be alive .
But -- but -- I could never care for any other man . ''
`` Oh , how interesting ! ''
sigh Wilhelmina .
`` I do so love sad love story .
But perhaps he will come back some day yet , Miss Holmes . ''
`` Oh , no , never now , '' I say , shake my head .

Or if he have n't , he have never forgive me . ''

But I felt already a change in the mental atmosphere surround me , and all through supper I be thrill with a secret exultation .
Repentant ?
Ashamed ?
Not a bit of it !
I 'd have do the same thing over again , and all I felt sorry for be that I have n't do it long ago .
When I get home that night Nancy look at me wonderingly , and say : `` You look like a girl to-night , Miss Charlotte . ''
`` I feel like one , '' I say laughing ; and I run to my room and do what I have never do before -- write a second poem in the same day .
I have to have some outlet for my feeling .
I call it `` In Summer Days of Long Ago , '' and I work Mary Gillespie 's rose and Cecil Fenwick 's eye into it , and make it so sad and reminiscent and minor-musicky that I felt perfectly happy .
For the next two month all go well and merrily .
Nobody ever say anything more to me about Cecil Fenwick , but the girl all chatter freely to me of their little love affair , and I become a sort of general confidant for them .
It just warm up the cockle of my heart , and I begin to enjoy the Sewing Circle famously .
I get a lot of pretty new dress and the dear hat , and I go everywhere I be ask and have a good time .
But there be one thing you can be perfectly sure of .
If you do wrong you be go to be punish for it sometime , somehow and somewhere .
My punishment be delay for two month , and then it descend on my head and I be crush to the very dust .
Another new family besides the Mercers have come to Avonlea in the spring -- the Maxwells .
There be just Mr. and Mrs. Maxwell ; they be a middle-aged couple and very well off .
Mr. Maxwell have buy the lumber mill , and they live up at the old Spencer place which have always be `` the '' place of Avonlea .
They live quietly , and Mrs. Maxwell hardly ever go anywhere because she be delicate .
She be out when I call and I be out when she return my call , so that I have never meet her .
It be the Sewing Circle day again -- at Sarah Gardiner 's this time .
I be late ; everybody else be there when I arrive , and the minute I enter the room I know something have happen , although I could n't imagine what .
Everybody look at me in the strange way .
Of course , Wilhelmina Mercer be the first to set her tongue go .
`` Oh , Miss Holmes , have you see him yet ? ''
she exclaim .
`` Seen whom ? ''
I say non-excitedly , get out my thimble and pattern .
`` Why , Cecil Fenwick .
He 's here -- in Avonlea -- visit his sister , Mrs. Maxwell . ''
I suppose I do what they expect me to do .
I drop everything I hold , and Josephine Cameron say afterwards that Charlotte Holmes would never be paler when she be in her coffin .
If they have just know why I turn so pale !
`` It 's impossible ! ''
I say blankly .
`` It 's really true , '' say Wilhelmina , delight at this development , a she suppose it , of my romance .
`` I be up to see Mrs. Maxwell last night , and I meet him . ''
`` It -- ca n't be -- the same -- Cecil Fenwick , '' I say faintly , because I have to say something .
`` Oh , yes , it be .
He belong in Blakely , New Brunswick , and he 's a lawyer , and he 's be out West twenty-two year .
He 's oh !
so handsome , and just a you describe him , except that his hair be quite gray .
He have never marry -- I ask Mrs. Maxwell -- so you see he have never forget you , Miss Holmes .
And , oh , I believe everything be go to come out all right . ''
I could n't exactly share her cheerful belief .
Everything seem to me to be come out most horribly wrong .
I be so mixed up I do n't know what to do or say .
I felt a if I be in a bad dream -- it MUST be a dream -- there could n't really be a Cecil Fenwick !
My feeling be simply indescribable .
Fortunately every one put my agitation down to quite a different cause , and they very kindly leave me alone to recover myself .
I shall never forget that awful afternoon .
Right after tea I excuse myself and go home as fast a I could go .
There I shut myself up in my room , but NOT to write poetry in my blank book .
No , indeed !
I felt in no poetical mood .
I try to look the fact squarely in the face .
There be a Cecil Fenwick , extraordinary a the coincidence be , and he be here in Avonlea .
All my friend -- and foe -- believe that he be the estranged lover of my youth .
If he stay long in Avonlea , one of two thing be bind to happen .
He would hear the story I have tell about him and deny it , and I would be hold up to shame and derision for the rest of my natural life ; or else he would simply go away in ignorance , and everybody would suppose he have forget me and would pity me maddeningly .
The latter possibility be bad enough , but it be n't to be compare to the former ; and oh , how I pray -- yes , I DID pray about it -- that he would go right away .
But Providence have other view for me .
Cecil Fenwick do n't go away .
He stay right on in Avonlea , and the Maxwells blossom out socially in his honor and try to give him a good time .
Mrs. Maxwell give a party for him .
I get a card -- but you may be very sure I do n't go , although Nancy think I be crazy not to .
Then every one else give party in honor of Mr. Fenwick and I be invite and never go .
Wilhelmina Mercer come and plead and scold and tell me if I avoid Mr. Fenwick like that he would think I still cherish bitterness against him , and he would n't make any advance towards a reconciliation .
Wilhelmina mean well , but she have n't a great deal of sense .
Cecil Fenwick seem to be a great favorite with everybody , young and old .
He be very rich , too , and Wilhelmina declare that half the girl be after him .
`` If it be n't for you , Miss Holmes , I believe I 'd have a try for him myself , in spite of his gray hair and quick temper -- for Mrs. Maxwell say he have a pretty quick temper , but it 's all over in a minute , '' say Wilhelmina , half in jest and wholly in earnest .
As for me , I give up go out at all , even to church .
I fret and pin and lose my appetite and never write a line in my blank book .
Nancy be half frantic and insist on dose me with her favorite patent pill .
I take them meekly , because it be a waste of time and energy to oppose Nancy , but , of course , they do n't do me any good .
My trouble be too deep-seated for pill to cure .
If ever a woman be punish for tell a lie I be that woman .
I stop my subscription to the Weekly Advocate because it still carry that wretched porous plaster advertisement , and I could n't bear to see it .
If it have n't be for that I would never have think of Fenwick for a name , and all this trouble would have be avert .
One evening , when I be mop in my room , Nancy come up .
`` There 's a gentleman in the parlor ask for you , Miss Charlotte . ''
My heart give just one horrible bounce .
`` What -- sort of a gentleman , Nancy ? ''
I falter .
`` I think it 's that Fenwick man that there 's be such a time about , '' say Nancy , who do n't know anything about my imaginary escapade , `` and he look to be mad clean through about something , for such a scowl I never see . ''
`` Tell him I 'll be down directly , Nancy , '' I say quite calmly .
As soon a Nancy have clump downstairs again I put on my lace fichu and put two hanky in my belt , for I think I 'd probably need more than one .
Then I hunt up an old Advocate for proof , and down I go to the parlor .
I know exactly how a criminal feel go to execution , and I 've be oppose to capital punishment ever since .
I open the parlor door and go in , carefully close it behind me , for Nancy have a deplorable habit of listen in the hall .
Then my leg give out completely , and I could n't have walk another step to save my life .
I just stand there , my hand on the knob , tremble like a leaf .
A man be stand by the south window look out ; he wheel around a I go in , and , a Nancy say , he have a scowl on and look angry clear through .
He be very handsome , and his gray hair give him such a distinguished look .
I recall this afterward , but just at the moment you may be quite sure I be n't think about it at all .
Then all at once a strange thing happen .
The scowl go right off his face and the anger out of his eye .
He look astonish , and then foolish .
I saw the color creep up into his cheek .
As for me , I still stand there star at him , not able to say a single word .
`` Miss Holmes , I presume , '' he say at last , in a deep , thrilling voice .
`` I -- I -- oh , confound it !
I have call -- I hear some foolish story and I come here in a rage .
I 've be a fool -- I know now they be n't true .
Just excuse me and I 'll go away and kick myself . ''
`` No , '' I say , find my voice with a gasp , `` you must n't go until you 've hear the truth .
It 's dreadful enough , but not as dreadful a you might otherwise think .
Those -- those story -- I have a confession to make .
I do tell them , but I do n't know there be such a person a Cecil Fenwick in existence . ''
He look puzzled , as well he might .
Then he smile , take my hand and lead me away from the door -- to the knob of which I be still hold with all my might -- to the sofa .
`` Let 's sit down and talk it over ` comfy , ' '' he say .
I just confess the whole shameful business .
It be terribly humiliate , but it serve me right .
I tell him how people be always twit me for never have have a beau , and how I have tell them I have ; and then I show him the porous plaster advertisement .
He hear me right through without a word , and then he throw back his big , curly , gray head and laugh .
`` This clear up a great many mysterious hint I 've be receive ever since I come to Avonlea , '' he say , `` and finally a Mrs. Gilbert come to my sister this afternoon with a long farrago of nonsense about the love affair I have once have with some Charlotte Holmes here .
She declare you have tell her about it yourself .
I confess I flame up .
I 'm a peppery chap , and I think -- I think -- oh , confound it , it might as well out : I think you be some lank old maid who be amuse herself tell ridiculous story about me .
When you come into the room I know that , whoever be to blame , you be not . ''
`` But I be , '' I say ruefully .
`` It be n't right of me to tell such a story -- and it be very silly , too .
But who would ever have suppose that there could be real Cecil Fenwick who have live in Blakely ?
I never heard of such a coincidence . ''
`` It 's more than a coincidence , '' say Mr. Fenwick decidedly .
`` It 's predestination ; that be what it be .
And now let 's forget it and talk of something else . ''
We talk of something else -- or at least Mr. Fenwick do , for I be too ashamed to say much -- so long that Nancy get restive and clump through the hall every five minute ; but Mr. Fenwick never take the hint .
When he finally go away he ask if he might come again .
`` It 's time we make up that old quarrel , you know , '' he say , laugh .
And I , an old maid of forty , catch myself blush like a girl .
But I felt like a girl , for it be such a relief to have that explanation all over .
I could n't even feel angry with Adella Gilbert .
She be always a mischief maker , and when a woman be bear that way she be more to be pity than blame .
I write a poem in the blank book before I go to sleep ; I have n't write anything for a month , and it be lovely to be at it once more .
Mr. Fenwick do come again -- the very next evening , but one .
And he come so often after that that even Nancy get resign to him .
One day I have to tell her something .
I shrink from do it , for I fear it would make her feel badly .
`` Oh , I 've be expect to hear it , '' she say grimly .
`` I felt the minute that man come into the house he bring trouble with him .
Well , Miss Charlotte , I wish you happiness .
I do n't know how the climate of California will agree with me , but I suppose I 'll have to put up with it . ''
`` But , Nancy , '' I say , `` I ca n't expect you to go away out there with me .
It 's too much to ask of you . ''
`` And where else would I be go ? ''
demanded Nancy in genuine astonishment .
`` How under the canopy could you keep house without me ?
I 'm not go to trust you to the mercy of a yellow Chinee with a pig-tail .
Where you go I go , Miss Charlotte , and there 's an end of it . ''
I be very glad , for I hat to think of part with Nancy even to go with Cecil .
As for the blank book , I have n't tell my husband about it yet , but I mean to some day .
And I 've subscribe for the Weekly Advocate again .
III .
HER FATHER 'S DAUGHTER `` We must invite your Aunt Jane , of course , '' say Mrs. Spencer .
Rachel make a protesting movement with her large , white , shapely hand -- hand which be so different from the thin , dark , twisted one fold on the table opposite her .
The difference be not cause by hard work or the lack of it ; Rachel have work hard all her life .
It be a difference inherent in temperament .
The Spencers , no matter what they do , or how hard they labor , all have plump , smooth , white hand , with firm , supple finger ; the Chiswicks , even those who toil not , neither do they spin , have hard , knot , twisted one .
Moreover , the contrast go deep than external , and twin itself with the innermost fiber of life , and think , and action .
`` I do n't see why we must invite Aunt Jane , '' say Rachel , with as much impatience a her soft , throaty voice could express .
`` Aunt Jane do n't like me , and I do n't like Aunt Jane . ''
`` I 'm sure I do n't see why you do n't like her , '' say Mrs. Spencer .
`` It 's ungrateful of you .
She have always be very kind to you . ''
`` She have always be very kind with one hand , '' smile Rachel .
`` I remember the first time I ever saw Aunt Jane .
I be six year old .
She hold out to me a small velvet pincushion with bead on it .
And then , because I do not , in my shyness , thank her quite as promptly a I should have do , she rap my head with her bethimbled finger to ` teach me good manner . '
It hurt horribly -- I 've always have a tender head .
And that have be Aunt Jane 's way ever since .
When I grow too big for the thimble treatment she use her tongue instead -- and that hurt bad .
And you know , mother , how she use to talk about my engagement .
She be able to spoil the whole atmosphere if she happen to come in a bad humor .
I do n't want her . ''
`` She must be invite .
People would talk so if she be n't . ''
`` I do n't see why they should .
She 's only my great-aunt by marriage .
I would n't mind in the least if people do talk .
They 'll talk anyway -- you know that , mother . ''
`` Oh , we must have her , '' say Mrs. Spencer , with the indifferent finality that mark all her word and decision -- a finality against which it be seldom of any avail to struggle .
People , who know , rarely attempt it ; stranger occasionally do , mislead by the deceit of appearance .
Isabella Spencer be a wisp of a woman , with a pale , pretty face , uncertainly-colored , long-lashed grayish eye , and great mass of dull , soft , silky brown hair .
She have delicate aquiline feature and a small , babyish red mouth .
She look a if a breath would sway her .
The truth be that a tornado would hardly have cause her to swerve an inch from her chosen path .
For a moment Rachel look rebellious ; then she yield , a she generally do in all difference of opinion with her mother .
It be not worth while to quarrel over the comparatively unimportant matter of Aunt Jane 's invitation .
A quarrel might be inevitable later on ; Rachel want to save all her resource for that .
She give her shoulder a shrug , and write Aunt Jane 's name down on the wedding list in her large , somewhat untidy handwriting -- a handwriting which always seem to irritate her mother .
Rachel never could understand this irritation .
She could never guess that it be because her writing look so much like that in a certain packet of faded letter which Mrs. Spencer keep at the bottom of an old horsehair trunk in her bedroom .
They be postmark from seaport all over the world .
Mrs. Spencer never read them or look at them ; but she remember every dash and curve of the handwriting .
Isabella Spencer have overcome many thing in her life by the sheer force and persistency of her will .
But she could not get the good of heredity .
Rachel be her father 's daughter at all point , and Isabella Spencer escape hat her for it only by love her the more fiercely because of it .
Even so , there be many time when she have to avert her eye from Rachel 's face because of the pang of the more subtle remembrance ; and never , since her child be bear , could Isabella Spencer bear to gaze on that child 's face in sleep .
Rachel be to be marry to Frank Bell in a fortnight 's time .
Mrs. Spencer be pleased with the match .
She be very fond of Frank , and his farm be so near to her own that she would not lose Rachel altogether .
Rachel fondly believe that her mother would not lose her at all ; but Isabella Spencer , wiser by olden experience , know what her daughter 's marriage must mean to her , and steel her heart to bear it with what fortitude she might .
They be in the sitting-room , decide on the wedding guest and other detail .
The September sunshine be come in through the wave bough of the apple tree that grow close up to the low window .
The glint waver over Rachel 's face , as white a a wood lily , with only a faint dream of rise in the cheek .
She wear her sleek , golden hair in a quaint arch around it .
Her forehead be very broad and white .
She be fresh and young and hopeful .
The mother 's heart contract in a spasm of pain a she look at her .
How like the girl be to -- to -- to the Spencers !
Those easy , curve outline , those large , mirthful blue eye , that finely mold chin !
Isabella Spencer shut her lip firmly and crush down some unbidden , unwelcome memory .
`` There will be about sixty guest , all tell , '' she say , a if she be think of nothing else .
`` We must move the furniture out of this room and set the supper-table here .
The dining-room be too small .
We must borrow Mrs. Bell 's fork and spoon .
She offer to lend them .
I 'd never have be willing to ask her .
The damask table cloth with the ribbon pattern must be bleach to-morrow .
Nobody else in Avonlea have such tablecloth .
And we 'll put the little dining-room table on the hall landing , upstairs , for the present . ''
Rachel be not think about the present , or the housewifely detail of the wedding .
Her breath be come quicker , and the faint blush on her smooth cheek have deepen to crimson .
She know that a critical moment be approach .
With a steady hand she write the last name on her list and draw a line under it .
`` Well , have you finish ? ''
ask her mother impatiently .
`` Hand it here and let me look over it to make sure that you have n't leave anybody out that should be in . ''
Rachel pass the paper across the table in silence .
The room seem to her to have grow very still .
She could hear the fly buzz on the pane , the soft purr of the wind about the low eaves and through the apple bough , the jerky beating of her own heart .
She felt frightened and nervous , but resolute .

But when she come to the last name , she do not utter it .
She cast a black glance at Rachel , and a spark leap up in the depth of the pale eye .
On her face be anger , amazement , incredulity , the last predominating .
The final name on the list of wed guest be the name of David Spencer .
David Spencer live alone in a little cottage down at the Cove .
He be a combination of sailor and fisherman .
He be also Isabella Spencer 's husband and Rachel 's father .
`` Rachel Spencer , have you take leave of your sens ?
What do you mean by such nonsense a this ? ''
`` I simply mean that I be go to invite my father to my wedding , '' answer Rachel quietly .
`` Not in my house , '' cry Mrs. Spencer , her lip as white a if her fiery tone have scathed them .

Her fright and nervousness be go .
Now that the conflict be actually on she find herself rather enjoy it .

She be not give to self-analysis , or she might have conclude that it be the sudden assertion of her own personality , so long dominate by her mother 's , which she be find so agreeable .

If I can not invite my father to see me married , no one else shall be invite . ''

In spite of her anger her heart thrill to it .
As never before , she realize that this girl be her own and her husband 's child , a live bond between them wherein their conflicting nature mingle and be reconcile .
She realize too , that Rachel , so long sweetly meek and obedient , meant to have her own way in this case -- and would have it .

He wo n't come . ''

She rise quickly and go upstairs to her own room , a dim little place shadow by the white birch grow thickly outside -- a virginal room , where everything bespeak the maiden .

Her heart , at this crisis in her life , yearn for her father , who be almost a stranger to her .
She know that her mother have probably speak the truth when she say that he would not come .
Rachel felt that her marriage vow would be lack in some indefinable sacredness if her father be not by to hear them speak .
Twenty-five year before this , David Spencer and Isabella Chiswick have be marry .
Spiteful people say there could be no doubt that Isabella have marry David for love , since he have neither land nor money to tempt her into a match of bargain and sale .
David be a handsome fellow , with the blood of a seafaring race in his vein .
He have be a sailor , like his father and grandfather before him ; but , when he marry Isabella , she induce him to give up the sea and settle down with her on a snug farm her father have leave her .
Isabella like farming , and love her fertile acre and opulent orchard .
She abhor the sea and all that pertain to it , less from any dread of it danger than from an inbred conviction that sailor be `` low '' in the social scale -- a specie of necessary vagabond .
In her eye there be a taint of disgrace in such a call .
David must be transform into a respectable , home-abiding tiller of broad land .
For five year all go well enough .
If , at time , David 's longing for the sea trouble him , he stifle it , and listen not to it luring voice .
He and Isabella be very happy ; the only drawback to their happiness lay in the regretted fact that they be childless .
Then , in the sixth year , come a crisis and a change .
Captain Barrett , an old crony of David 's , want him to go with him on a voyage a mate .
At the suggestion all David 's long-repressed craving for the wide blue waste of the ocean , and the wind whistle through the spar with the salt foam in it breath , break forth with a passion all the more intense for that very repression .
He must go on that voyage with James Barrett -- he MUST !
That over , he would be content again ; but go he must .
His soul struggle within him like a fettered thing .
Isabella oppose the scheme vehemently and unwisely , with mordant sarcasm and unjust reproach .
The latent obstinacy of David 's character come to the support of his longing -- a longing which Isabella , with five generation of land-loving ancestry behind her , could not understand at all .
He be determine to go , and he tell Isabella so .
`` I 'm sick of plow and milk cow , '' he say hotly .

`` What do you want here ? ''
she say , in the tone she be accustom to use to tramp and Syrian peddler .

Why , I -- I -- want my wife .
I 've come home . ''

I 'm no wife of yours .

When the scandalized Chiswicks , Aunt Jane at their head , try to patch up the matter with argument and entreaty , Isabella meet them stonily , seem not to hear what they say , and make no response .
She worst them totally .

Why be this ?
Rachel go straight to her mother , put one little dimpled hand on Isabella Spencer 's knee , look up with great search blue eye , and say gravely , `` Mother , why have n't I get a father like the other little girl ? ''

She understand clearly and hopelessly that she could never have a father -- that , in this respect , she must always be unlike other people .
`` Your father care nothing for you , '' say Isabella Spencer in conclusion .

You must never speak of him to anybody again . ''

She be an imaginative child , and in fancy she make the acquaintance of her father .
She have never see him , but he be more real to her than most of the people she have see .

And the tone in which she say `` father '' be soft and more tender than the one which voice `` mother . ''

`` Here be something for you , Rachel .

IV .

So she have not run .
Miss Rosetta always run if anybody call and her front hair be in curl-papers ; and , though the errand of the say caller might be life or death , he or she have to wait until Miss Rosetta have take her hair out .
Everybody in Avonlea know this , because everybody in Avonlea know everything about everybody else .
But Mr. Patterson have wheel into the lane so quickly and unexpectedly that Miss Rosetta have have no time to run ; so , twitch off the checked apron , she stand her ground as calmly a might be under the disagreeable consciousness of curl-papers .

`` Charlotte have get another spell with her heart !
I know it !
I 've be expect to hear it !

-- that your sister , Mrs. Wheeler , have have a letter from a cousin of yours , and she 's in Charlottetown .

I be the old .

She get marry the same way .

Jane die ! ''

I 'll show her !

No answer .
Miss Rosetta try the door .
It be lock .

There be nothing else for her to do .

she exclaim .

Only come . ''

THE DREAM-CHILD A man 's heart -- aye , and a woman 's , too -- should be light in the spring .
The spirit of resurrection be abroad , call the life of the world out of it wintry grave , knock with radiant finger at the gate of it tomb .
It stir in human heart , and make them glad with the old primal gladness they felt in childhood .
It quicken human soul , and bring them , if so they will , so close to God that they may clasp hand with Him .
It be a time of wonder and renew life , and a great outward and inward rapture , a of a young angel softly clap his hand for creation 's joy .
At least , so it should be ; and so it always have be with me until the spring when the dream-child first come into our life .
That year I hat the spring -- I , who have always love it so .
As boy I have love it , and a man .
All the happiness that have ever be mine , and it be much , have come to blossom in the springtime .
It be in the spring that Josephine and I have first love each other , or , at least , have first come into the full knowledge that we love .
I think that we must have love each other all our life , and that each succeed spring be a word in the revelation of that love , not to be understood until , in the fullness of time , the whole sentence be write out in that most beautiful of all beautiful spring .
How beautiful it be !
And how beautiful she be !
I suppose every lover think that of his lass ; otherwise he be a poor sort of lover .
But it be not only my eye of love that make my dear lovely .
She be slim and lithe a a young , white-stemmed birch tree ; her hair be like a soft , dusky cloud ; and her eye be as blue a Avonlea harbor on a fair twilight , when all the sky be abloom over it .
She have dark lash , and a little red mouth that quiver when she be very sad or very happy , or when she love very much -- quiver like a crimson rise too rudely shake by the wind .
At such time what be a man to do save kiss it ?
The next spring we be marry , and I bring her home to my gray old homestead on the gray old harbor shore .
A lonely place for a young bride , say Avonlea people .
Nay , it be not so .
She be happy here , even in my absence .
She love the great , restless harbor and the vast , misty sea beyond ; she love the tide , keep their world-old tryst with the shore , and the gull , and the croon of the wave , and the call of the wind in the fir wood at noon and even ; she love the moonrises and the sunset , and the clear , calm night when the star seem to have fall into the water and to be a little dizzy from such a fall .
She love these thing , even a I do .
No , she be never lonely here then .
The third spring come , and our boy be bear .
We think we have be happy before ; now we know that we have only dream a pleasant dream of happiness , and have awaken to this exquisite reality .
We think we have love each other before ; now , a I look into my wife 's pale face , blanch with it baptism of pain , and meet the uplifted gaze of her blue eye , aglow with the holy passion of motherhood , I know we have only imagine what love might be .
The imagination have be sweet , a the thought of the rise be sweet before the bud be open ; but a the rise to the thought , so be love to the imagination of it .
`` All my thought be poetry since baby come , '' my wife say once , rapturously .

I think I grieve over my little son 's death a deeply and sincerely a ever man do , or could .
But the heart of the father be not a the heart of the mother .
Time bring no healing to Josephine ; she fret and pin ; her cheek lose their pretty oval , and her red mouth grow pale and drooping .
I hop that spring might work it miracle upon her .
When the bud swell , and the old earth grow green in the sun , and the gull come back to the gray harbor , whose very grayness grow golden and mellow , I think I should see her smile again .
But , when the spring come , come the dream-child , and the fear that be to be my companion , at bed and board , from sunsetting to sunsetting .
One night I awaken from sleep , realize in the moment of awaken that I be alone .
I listen to hear whether my wife be move about the house .
I hear nothing but the little splash of wave on the shore below and the low moan of the distant ocean .
I rise and search the house .
She be not in it .
I do not know where to seek her ; but , at a venture , I start along the shore .
It be pale , fainting moonlight .
The harbor look like a phantom harbor , and the night be a still and cold and calm a the face of a dead man .
At last I saw my wife come to me along the shore .
When I saw her , I know what I have fear and how great my fear have be .
As she draw near , I saw that she have be cry ; her face be stain with tear , and her dark hair hang loose over her shoulder in little , glossy ringlet like a child 's .
She seem to be very tired , and at interval she wring her small hand together .

`` I do my best -- I hurry so ; but he be always a little way ahead .
And then I lose him -- and so I come back .
But I do my best -- indeed I do .
And oh , I be so tired ! ''
`` Josie , dear , what do you mean , and where have you be ? ''
I say , draw her close to me .
`` Why do you go out so -- alone in the night ? ''
She look at me wonderingly .
`` How could I help it , David ?
He call me .
I have to go . ''
`` WHO call you ? ''
`` The child , '' she answer in a whisper .
`` Our child , David -- our pretty boy .
I awaken in the darkness and hear him call to me down on the shore .
Such a sad , little wail cry , David , a if he be cold and lonely and want his mother .

I could only hear the call , and I follow it on and on , far down the shore .
Oh , I try so hard to overtake it , but I could not .
Once I saw a little white hand beckoning to me far ahead in the moonlight .
But still I could not go fast enough .
And then the cry cease , and I be there all alone on that terrible , cold , gray shore .
I be so tired and I come home .
But I wish I could have find him .
Perhaps he do not know that I try to .
Perhaps he think his mother never listen to his call .
Oh , I would not have him think that . ''

You can not understand -- you be only his father .

It be not you who pay the price of his dear life in pain .

I keep a grim vigil with dread .

I have smile at the story then .

Wait for me .
Mother be come to her pretty boy ! ''

What a horror brood over that spring -- that so beautiful spring !
It be a time of wonder and marvel ; of the soft touch of silver rain on green field ; of the incredible delicacy of young leaf ; of blossom on the land and blossom in the sunset .
The whole world bloom in a flush and tremor of maiden loveliness , instinct with all the evasive , fleeting charm of spring and girlhood and young morning .
And almost every night of this wonderful time the dream-child call his mother , and we rove the gray shore in quest of him .

Then follow it she would , even through storm and darkness .
It be then , she say , that the cry sound loud and nearest , a if her pretty boy be frighten by the tempest .

We have no near relative -- none with any right to share any trouble -- and whoso accepteth human love must bind it to his soul with pain .

He look grave when he hear my story .
I do not like his expression nor his few guarded remark .
He say he think human aid would avail little ; she might come all right in time ; humor her , as far a possible , watch over her , protect her .
He need not to tell me THAT .

I know that suspicion be be whisper from lip to lip .
We have be see on our nightly quest .
Men and woman begin to look at u pityingly when we go abroad .

I know then that the end be near ; the end have be near in the old grandmother 's case sixty year before when the dream-child call in the day .

I could not watch by day and night .
Unless I have assistance I would break down .
I do not think that I should .
Love be strong than that .
And on one thing I be determine -- they should never take my wife from me .
No restraint sterner than a husband 's loving hand should ever be put upon her , my pretty , piteous darling .
I never speak of the dream-child to her .
The doctor advise against it .
It would , he say , only serve to deepen the delusion .

This pain , that never leave me , would leave me than .

I be come to you .
